Actions on Mount Safa Before Sa'y
Ruling on climbing Safa, facing Kaaba, and supplicating before Sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts performed on Mount Safa before Sa'y and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Climbing Safa, facing Kaaba, and supplicating are sunnah; the Prophet's fi'l is the proof.

This passage from al-Hidayah details the recommended actions a pilgrim performs on Mount Safa immediately before beginning the Sa'y between Safa and Marwa. These actions are established by the hadith of Jabir and include climbing to see the Kaaba, glorifying Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, raising hands, and supplicating. The text also clarifies a common misunderstanding regarding the exit door from the mosque.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of acts
List the actions the pilgrim does on Safa: climbing, facing the Kaaba, takbir, tahlil, salawat, raising hands, and supplication. Note the order and the legal ruling (sunnah/mustahabb).
These acts are sunnah, not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author cites the hadith of Jabir (recorded by Muslim) that the Prophet climbed Safa until he saw the House, then stood facing the qibla and supplicated. This is the dalil for the sunnah acts.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but the meaning is clear.
3
Understand the talil (reasoning)
The text explains why praise and salawat precede supplication: to bring the du'a closer to acceptance, as done in other contexts.
This is based on general practice, not a specific proof.
4
Analyze the purpose of climbing
The author specifies climbing only until the Kaaba is visible because the goal is istiqbal (facing the House). Thus, the extent is a means, not an end.
Excessive climbing beyond need is not required.
5
Distinguish the ruling on exiting the mosque
The Prophet used Bab al-Safa because it was the closest door. This makes it mustahabb (recommended), not sunnah. Using any other door is equally valid.
This refutes the view that using Bab al-Safa is a fixed sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهِ وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْبَيْتَ وَيُكَبِّرُ وَيُهَلِلُ وَيُصَلِّى عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ وَيَدْعُو الله لِحَاجَتِهِ لِمَارُوى أنَّ النبيَّ صَعِدَ الصَّفَا حَتَّى إِذَا نَظَرَ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ قَامَ مُسْتَقبَلَ الْقِبْلَةِ يَدْعُو الله ولأنَّ الثَّناء وَالصَّلوةَ يُقَدِ مَان عَلَى الدُّعَاءِ تَقْرِيبًا إِلَى الْإِجَابَةِ كَمَا فِي غَيْرِهِ مِنَ الدَّعْوَاتِ وَالرَّفَعُ سُنَّةُ الدُّعَاءِ وَإِنَّمَا يَصْعَدُ بقَدْرِ مَا يَصِيرُ البَيْتَ بِمَرْأى مِنْهُ لأنَّ الإِسْتِقْبَالَ هُوَ الْمَقْصُودُ بِالصُّعُودِ وَ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا مِنْ أَيِّ بَابِ شَاءَ وَإِنَّمَا خَرَجَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مِنْ بَابِ بَنِى مَخْرُومٍ وَهُوَ الَّذِي يُسَمَّى بَابِ الصَّفَا لِأَنَّهُ كَانَ أَقْرَبَ الْأَبْوَابِ إِلَى الصُّفَا لَا لِأَنَّهُ سُنَّةٌ
ترجمہ کہا کہ پھر کو ہ صفا کی طرف نکلے پس صفا پر چڑھے اور بیت اللہ کی طرف منہ کرے اور تکبیر وتہلیل کرے۔ اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود بھیجے اور اپنے دونوں ہاتھ اٹھائے۔ اور اپنی ضرورت کے لئے اللہ سے مانگے ۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم صفا پر چڑھے حتی کہ جب آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بیت اللہ کو دیکھا تو قبلہ رخ کھڑے ہو کر اللہ سے دعا کرنے لگے۔ اور اس لئے کہ ثناء اور درودونوں دعا پر مقدم کئے جائیں گے دعا کو قبولیت سے قریب تر کرنے کے لئے۔ جیسے دوسری دعاؤں میں ہوتا ہے۔ اور ہاتھ اٹھانا دعا کی سنت ہے اور صفا پر اس قدر چڑھے کہ بیت اللہ اس کی نظر کے سامنے ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ صفا پر چڑھنے سے استقبال ہی مقصود ہے۔ اور صفا کی طرف جس دروازہ سے چاہے نکلے۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم باب بنی مخزوم جس کو باب صفا کہا جاتا ہے، سے نکلے اس لئے کہ یہی دروازہ دوسرے دروازوں کی بہ نسبت صفا سے زیادہ قریب ہے۔ اس لئے نہیں کہ یہ سنت ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ طواف قدوم سے فارغ ہو کر سعی بین الصفا والمروہ کے لئے نکلے چنانچہ پہلے صفا پر چڑھ کر بیت اللہ کا استقبال کرے۔ اور تکبیر اور لا الہ الا اللہ کہے اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود پڑھے۔ اور ہاتھ اٹھا کر خداوند قدوس سے دعا کرے۔ کیونکہ امام مسلم کے بیان کے مطابق حدیث جابر میں یہ مضمون مذکور ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم صفا پر چڑھے حتی کہ جب بیت اللہ کو دیکھا تو قبلہ رخ کھڑے ہو کر اللہ سے دعا کی۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثنا اور درود کو دعا پر اس لئے مقدم کیا جاتا ہے تا کہ دعا قبولیت سے قریب تر ہو جائے جیسا کہ دوسرے اوقات میں دعا سے پہلے ثنا اور در و دعلی النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اس مقصد سے پڑھا جاتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ کوہ صفا پر اس قدر چڑ ھے کہ بیت اللہ اس کی نظروں کے سامنے آجائے ۔ کیونکہ صفا پر چڑھنے سے مقصود بیت اللہ کا استقبال ہے اور یہ مقصود اسی صورت میں حاصل ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ صفا کی طرف جانے کے لئے حاجی کو اختیار ہے کہ جس دروازہ سے چاہے نکلے اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم باب بنو مخزوم سے نکلے تھے ۔ باب بنو مخزوم کو باب صفا بھی کہتے ہیں۔ اس دروازہ سے آپ کا نکلنا اس لئے تھا کہ یہ دروازہ کو وصفا سے قریب تر ہے۔ پس اس دروازہ سے نکلنا مستحب ہوگا نہ کہ سنت ۔ جیسا کہ امام شافعی باب صفا
He said: Then he goes out to Safa, climbs upon it, faces the House, says Allahu Akbar and La ilaha illa Allah, sends blessings upon the Prophet, raises his hands, and supplicates Allah for his need. Because it is narrated that the Prophet climbed Safa, and when he looked at the House, he stood facing the qibla supplicating Allah. And because praise and prayers are advanced before supplication to bring it closer to acceptance, as in other supplications. Raising the hands is a sunnah of supplication. He climbs only to the extent that the House becomes visible to him, because facing it is the purpose of climbing. He goes out to Safa from any door he wishes. The Prophet went out from the door of Banu Makhzum, which is called Bab al-Safa, because it was the closest door to Safa, not because it is a sunnah. Translation: He said: Then he goes out to Mount Safa, so he climbs on it, faces the House of Allah, says takbir and tahlil, sends blessings on the Messenger of Allah, raises his hands, and asks Allah for his need. Because it is narrated that the Prophet climbed Safa until when he saw the House, he stood facing the qibla and began supplicating Allah. And because praise and blessings are advanced before supplication to bring it closer to acceptance, as in other supplications. Raising the hands is the sunnah of supplication. He climbs only to the extent that the House comes into his sight, because facing it is the purpose of climbing. He goes out to Safa from any door he wishes. The Prophet went out from Bab Bani Makhzum, which is called Bab al-Safa, because it was closer to Safa than other doors, not because it is a sunnah. Explanation: The issue is that after finishing Tawaf al-Qudum, he goes out for Sa'y between Safa and Marwa. So first he climbs Safa, faces the Kaaba, says takbir and La ilaha illa Allah, recites salawat on the Prophet, raises his hands, and supplicates to Allah. Because according to the narration of Imam Muslim in the hadith of Jabir, it is mentioned that the Prophet climbed Safa, and when he saw the House, he stood facing the qibla and supplicated to Allah. The second proof is that praise and salawat are advanced before supplication so that the supplication becomes closer to acceptance, just as at other times, praise and salawat on the Prophet are recited before supplication for this purpose. The author of al-Hidayah says: He should climb Mount Safa to the extent that the House comes before his eyes, because the purpose of climbing Safa is to face the House, and this purpose is achieved in this manner. The author of al-Hidayah states: The pilgrim has the choice to go out to Safa from any door he wishes. The Prophet went out from Bab Bani Makhzum, which is also called Bab al-Safa. His going out from this door was because it was the closest door to Safa. Therefore, going out from this door is mustahabb (recommended), not a sunnah (established practice) as Imam Shafi'i might hold regarding Bab al-Safa.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the actions to be performed on Mount Safa before beginning the Sa'y. The matn outlines the sequence: after completing Tawaf al-Qudum, the pilgrim goes to Safa, climbs it until the Kaaba is visible, faces the House, utters takbir and tahlil, sends salawat on the Prophet, raises his hands, and makes personal supplications. The proof is the hadith of Jabir recorded by Muslim showing the Prophet's practice. The reasoning (talil) is that praise and salawat precede supplication to increase its likelihood of acceptance. Raising hands is the sunnah of supplication. The author specifies climbing just enough to see the House because facing it is the goal. Regarding the exit from the mosque to Safa, the text clarifies that any door is permissible; the Prophet used Bab al-Safa because it was closest, making it mustahabb but not sunnah. This refutes the notion that using that particular door is an obligatory sunnah.

Key Terms
صفا (Safa): One of the two hills between which Sa'y is performed; the starting point of Sa'y.
تکبیر (takbir): Saying Allahu Akbar.
تہلیل (tahlil): Saying La ilaha illa Allah.
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands in supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, why did the Prophet use Bab al-Safa when going out to Safa?
A) It was a divine command
B) It was the closest door to Safa
C) It was the only door available
D) It is a sunnah that must be followed

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts on Safa are climbing, facing the Kaaba, takbir, tahlil, salawat, raising hands, and supplication; the exit door is flexible, with Bab al-Safa being merely recommended.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Recommended Actions on Safa after Tawaf al-Qudum
Explains sunnah actions on Safa after Tawaf al-Qudum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions on Safa and explain why exiting from Bab al-Safa is mustahabb, not a confirmed sunnah.

Core Idea
Facing the Kaaba on Safa is sunnah; the door used is just a convenience, not a ritual.

After completing Tawaf al-Qudum, the pilgrim proceeds to Sa'y between Safa and Marwah. The first step is ascending Safa. This lesson explains the recommended actions (sunan) at that moment, based on the Prophet's practice and Hanafi legal reasoning. Distinguishing between what is sunnah and what is merely recommended is key to proper fiqh understanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
List the actions the pilgrim performs on Safa according to the text: facing the Kaaba, saying takbir and tahlil, sending blessings on the Prophet, raising hands, and making du'a.
These are all sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir in Sahih Muslim, where the Prophet ascended Safa, faced the Kaaba, and made du'a. The Hanafi school uses this fi'l (action) to derive recommendation (nadb).
The hadith is ahad (singular) and zanni in both transmission and indication.
3
Understand the purpose of ascending
The text explains that the pilgrim should climb only enough to see the Kaaba, because the purpose is to face it (istiqbal).
Excessive climbing is not recommended.
4
Analyse the ruling on the door
The Prophet came out from Bab al-Safa (door of Banu Makhzum) because it was the closest door, not as a ritual act. Therefore, using that door is mustahabb (recommended) but not a confirmed sunnah.
This refutes the Shafi'i view that it is a fixed sunnah.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i considers the door a sunnah based on the Prophet's action. The Hanafi response distinguishes between a practice done for convenience and one done for ritual purpose.
The practical difference: Hanafis allow any door; Shafi'is prefer Bab al-Safa as sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفا پر چڑھ کر کون سے اعمال کرے

قَالَ ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهِ وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْبَيْتَ وَيُكَبِّرُ وَيُهَلِلُ وَيُصَلِّى عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ وَيَدْعُو الله لِحَاجَتِهِ لِمَارُوى أنَّ النبيَّ صَعِدَ الصَّفَا حَتَّى إِذَا نَظَرَ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ قَامَ مُسْتَقْبلَ الْقِبْلَةِ يَدْعُو الله ولأنَّ الثَّناء وَالصَّلوةَ يُقَدِ مَان عَلَى الدُّعَاءِ تَقْرِيبًا إِلَى الْإِجَابَةِ كَمَا فِي غَيْرِهِ مِنَ الدَّعْوَاتِ وَالرَّفَعُ سُنَّةُ الدُّعَاءِ وَإِنَّمَا يَصْعَدُ بقَدْرِ مَا يَصِيرُ البَيْتَ بِمَرْأى مِنْهُ لأنَّ الإِسْتِقْبَالَ هُوَ الْمَقْصُودُ بِالصُّعُودِ وَ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا مِنْ أَيِّ بَابِ شَاءَ وَإِنَّمَا خَرَجَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مِنْ بَابِ بَنِى مَخْرُومٍ وَهُوَ الَّذِي يُسَمَّى بَابِ الصَّفَا لِأَنَّهُ كَانَ أَقْرَبَ الْأَبْوَابِ إِلَى الصُفَا لَا لِأَنَّهُ سُنَّةٌ

ترجمہ کہا کہ پھر کو ہ صفا کی طرف نکلے پس صفا پر چڑھے اور بیت اللہ کی طرف منہ کرے اور تکبیر وتہلیل کرے۔ اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود بھیجے اور اپنے دونوں ہاتھ اٹھائے۔ اور اپنی ضرورت کے لئے اللہ سے مانگے ۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم صفا پر چڑھے حتی کہ جب آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بیت اللہ کو دیکھا تو قبلہ رخ کھڑے ہو کر اللہ سے دعا کرنے لگے۔ اور اس لئے کہ ثناء اور درودونوں دعا پر مقدم کئے جائیں گے دعا کو قبولیت سے قریب تر کرنے کے لئے۔ جیسے دوسری دعاؤں میں ہوتا ہے۔ اور ہاتھ اٹھانا دعا کی سنت ہے اور صفا پر اس قدر چڑھے کہ بیت اللہ اس کی نظر کے سامنے ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ صفا پر چڑھنے سے استقبال ہی مقصود ہے۔ اور صفا کی طرف جس دروازہ سے چاہے نکلے۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم باب بنی مخزوم جس کو باب صفا کہا جاتا ہے، سے نکلے اس لئے کہ یہی دروازہ دوسرے دروازوں کی بہ نسبت صفا سے زیادہ قریب ہے۔ اس لئے نہیں کہ یہ سنت ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ طواف قدوم سے فارغ ہو کر سعی بین الصفا والمروہ کے لئے نکلے چنانچہ پہلے صفا پر چڑھ کر بیت اللہ کا استقبال کرے۔ اور تکبیر اور لا الہ الا اللہ کہے اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود پڑھے۔ اور ہاتھ اٹھا کر خداوند قدوس سے دعا کرے۔ کیونکہ امام مسلم کے بیان کے مطابق حدیث جابر میں یہ مضمون مذکور ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم صفا پر چڑھے حتی کہ جب بیت اللہ کو دیکھا تو قبلہ رخ کھڑے ہو کر اللہ سے دعا کی۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثنا اور درود کو دعا پر اس لئے مقدم کیا جاتا ہے تا کہ دعا قبولیت سے قریب تر ہو جائے جیسا کہ دوسرے اوقات میں دعا سے پہلے ثنا اور در و دعلی النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اس مقصد سے پڑھا جاتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ کوہ صفا پر اس قدر چڑ ھے کہ بیت اللہ اس کی نظروں کے سامنے آجائے ۔ کیونکہ صفا پر چڑھنے سے مقصود بیت اللہ کا استقبال ہے اور یہ مقصود اسی صورت میں حاصل ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ صفا کی طرف جانے کے لئے حاجی کو اختیار ہے کہ جس دروازہ سے چاہے نکلے اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم باب بنو مخزوم سے نکلے تھے ۔ باب بنو مخزوم کو باب صفا بھی کہتے ہیں۔ اس دروازہ سے آپ کا نکلنا اس لئے تھا کہ یہ دروازہ کو وصفا سے قریب تر ہے۔ پس اس دروازہ سے نکلنا مستحب ہوگا نہ کہ سنت ۔ جیسا کہ امام شافعی باب صفا
He said: Then he goes out to al-Safa, and ascends it, and faces the House (Kaaba), and says Takbir and Tahlil, and sends blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), and raises his hands, and makes du'a to Allah for his need. Because it is narrated that the Prophet (saw) ascended al-Safa until, when he looked at the House, he stood facing the qibla, making du'a to Allah. And because praise and salutation are presented before du'a to bring it closer to acceptance, as in other du'as. Raising the hands is the sunnah of du'a. He ascends only to the extent that the House becomes visible to him, because facing (the House) is the purpose of ascending. He goes out to al-Safa from whichever door he wishes. The Prophet (saw) came out from the door of Banu Makhzum, which is called the Door of al-Safa, because it was the closest of the doors to al-Safa, not because it is sunnah.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This is an expansion of the matn by al-Hidayah. It explains the recommended actions (sunan) after completing Tawaf al-Qudum. The pilgrim should proceed to Safa, climb until he can see the Kaaba, face it, praise Allah (Takbir and Tahlil), send blessings upon the Prophet, raise hands, and make personal dua. The proof is the hadith of Jabir (Muslim) and the reasoning that praise and salawat precede dua to increase acceptance. The pilgrim only needs to climb high enough to see the Kaaba. Regarding the door, the Prophet used Bab al-Safa (door of Banu Makhzum) because it was closest; thus using it is mustahabb, not a confirmed sunnah. This refutes the Shafi'i view that it is a fixed sunnah.

Key Terms
صَفا (Safa): A hill near the Kaaba, one of the two starting points for sa'y between Safa and Marwah.
طواف قدوم (Tawaf al-Qudum): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Makkah by non-residents.
سعي (Sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of ascending Safa according to the text?
A) To see the mountains of Mina
B) To face the Kaaba and make supplication
C) To perform Tawaf al-Qudum
D) To greet the residents of Makkah

Key Takeaway
The actions on Safa are sunnah; the choice of door is not sunnah but simply the closest door.

The Manner of Sa'y and the Counting of Shawt
Describes actions and defines shawt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prescribed actions of sa'y between Safa and Marwah, explain the Hanafi definition of a shawt, and distinguish it from Imam al-Tahawi's view.

Core Idea
One shawt is one leg from Safa to Marwah or vice versa, not the round trip.

Sa'y between Safa and Marwah is a wajib act of Hajj and Umrah. In this passage from al-Hidayah, Imam al-Marghinani details the sunnah manner of performing sa'y—walking dignifiedly, then running between the green markers—and clarifies a key dispute about what constitutes one shawt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions per leg
Read the description of the pilgrim's movement from Safa to Marwah: descending, walking normally, running in the valley between the green markers, then walking again and ascending Marwah.
These actions are repeated for each leg, but on the return leg, the running is again performed in the same valley area.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith of the Prophet's practice as transmitted by Jabir and others: he descended from Safa, walked, ran in Batn al-Wadi, walked again, and ascended Marwah, making seven circuits.
The hadith establishes both the manner and the count.
3
Define a shawt
The author explicitly states: 'Wa hadha shawtun wahid' (And this is one shawt), referring to the leg from Safa to Marwah. This means the return leg is a separate shawt.
Thus, one full circuit (Safa->Marwah->Safa) comprises two shawt.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam al-Tahawi held that a round trip (Safa to Marwah and back) is one shawt. The author of al-Hidayah rejects this and insists each direction is a shawt.
The dispute affects the total count: seven shawt per sa'y under al-Hidayah, fourteen under Tahawi.
5
Understand the tarjih
The author prefers al-Hidayah's view because all companions' reports agree that the Prophet made seven circuits (ashwat), not fourteen. Therefore, each leg must be a shawt.
This tarjih is based on the unanimity of the narrations.

Source Text

قَالَ ثُمَّ يَنْحِطُ نَحوَ الْمَرْوَةِ وَ يَمْشِي عَلى هَيْتِهِ فَإِذَا بَلَغَ بَطْنَ الْوَادِى يَسْعَى بَيْنَ الْمُلَيْنِ الْأَخْصَرَينِ سَعيًا ثُمَّ يَمْشِي عَلى هَذَيْتِهِ حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ الْمَرْوَةَ وَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا وَيَفْعَلُ كَمَا فَعَلَ عَلَى الصَّفَا لِمَارُوى أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَزَلَ مِنَ الصَّفَا وَجَعَلَ يَمْشِي نَحْوَ الْمَرْوَةِ وَسَعَى فِي بَطْنِ الْوَادِى حَتَّى إِذَا خَرَجَ مِنْ بَطْنِ الْوَادِى مَشَى حَتَّى صَعِدَ الْمَرْوَةَ وَطَافَ بَيْنَهُمَا سُبعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ وَهَذَا شَوطُ وَاحِدٌ

ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ پھر مروہ کی جانب اتر کر سکون کے ساتھ پر وقار انداز میں چلے پھرے جب بطن وادی میں پہنچے تو دونوں سبز میلین کے درمیان تھوڑا سا دوڑے۔ پھر سکون کے ساتھ پر وقار طریقہ سے چلے، یہاں تک کہ مروہ پر آ جائے اور اس پر چڑھے اور کرے جیسا کہ صفا پر کیا تھا۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم صفا سے اترے اور مروہ کی طرف چلنے لگے ۔ اور بطن وادی میں سعی کی جہتی کہ جب بطن وادی سے نکلے تو چلے یہاں تک کہ مردہ پر چڑھے اور ان دونوں کے درمیان سات پھیرے ( چکر لگائے ۔ اور یہ ایک شرط ہے۔ تشریح امام قدوری نے فرمایا کہ صفا سے مروہ کی طرف اترے اور انتہائی سکون اور وقار کے ساتھ چلے۔ پس جب بطن وادی میں پہنچے تو میلین اخضرین کے درمیان سعی کرے۔ پھر سکون کے ساتھ چل کر مردہ پر آجائے اور اس پر چڑھ جائے اور جو کام کو صفا پر کیا تھا وہی مردہ پر کرے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے جس کو صاحب ہدایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ صفا سے چل کر مروہ پر جانا ایک شوط ہے اور مروہ سے صفا کی طرف لوٹ کر آنا دوسرا شوط ہے۔ امام طحاوی نے فرمایا ہے کہ صفا سے مروہ پر جانا اور مروہ سے صفا کی طرف لوٹ کر آنا یہ ایک شوط ہے۔ لیکن اصح قول وہ ہے جس کو صاحب ہدایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے افعال حج کو روایت کرنے والے تمام حضرات صحابہ کا اس پر اتفاق ہے کہ آپ نے صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سات چکر لگائے ۔ اور امام طحاوی کے بیان کے مطابق بجائے سات کے چودہ شوط ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اس لئے صاحب ہدایہ کا بیان کردہ قول ہی اصح معلوم ہوتا ہے۔
He said: Then he descends towards al-Marwah, and walks in his normal manner. When he reaches the middle of the valley, he runs between the two green markers, then continues walking in his normal manner until he reaches al-Marwah, and ascends it, and does as he did on al-Safa, because it is narrated that the Prophet (saw) descended from al-Safa and began walking towards al-Marwah, and he ran in the middle of the valley until he emerged from the middle of the valley, then walked until he ascended al-Marwah, and he made seven circuits between them. And this is one shawt.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage from al-Hidayah explains the actions from Safa to Marwah. The pilgrim descends from Safa and walks with dignity to the valley floor, then runs between the two green markers (al-milayni al-akhdarayn). After exiting the valley, he resumes normal walking until reaching Marwah, where he ascends and repeats the same actions as on Safa. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet's practice. The commentary also clarifies the definition of a shawt: according to the author of al-Hidayah, one shawt is from Safa to Marwah, and the return from Marwah to Safa is another shawt. This differs from Imam al-Tahawi, who considered the round trip as one shawt. The text favors al-Hidayah's view because it aligns with the unanimous report that the Prophet made seven circuits (ashwat) between them, not fourteen. Thus, each leg is a separate shawt.

Key Terms
بطن الوادي (Batn al-Wadi): The valley floor between Safa and Marwah where running is prescribed.
الميلين الأخضرين (Al-Milayni al-Akhdarayn): The two green markers that delineate the area where sa'y (running) is performed.
شوط (Shawt): One leg from Safa to Marwah or from Marwah to Safa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Hidayah, where does the pilgrim run during sa'y?
A) From Safa to Marwah entirely
B) Between the two green markers in Batn al-Wadi
C) From the start of the valley to the top of Marwah
D) Only when ascending Marwah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, each leg from Safa to Marwah or vice versa is one shawt, and sa'y consists of seven shawt performed with walking except for the running between the two green markers.

Ruling on Sa'y: Wajib Not Rukn (Shafi'i Dispute)
Establishes sa'y as wajib (not rukn) and refutes Shafi'i proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sa'y (it is wajib, not rukn), explain the evidence from Quran 2:158 and the Shafi'i hadith, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of omitting sa'y in both schools.

Core Idea
Sa'y is wajib, not rukn, because a pillar requires decisive (qat'i) proof, and the Quranic phrase 'no blame' negates pillar status.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a key dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the nature of sa'y in Hajj. Is it a pillar (rukn) whose omission invalidates the pilgrimage, or an obligatory act (wajib) that requires compensation? The Hanafi school, basing its argument on the Quranic verse 'no blame' (2:158), holds that sa'y cannot be a rukn, yet it remains obligatory through other evidence. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rulings of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that sa'y is wajib, not a rukn. What does this mean in practice?
Wajib in Hanafi: omission requires dam (sacrifice) but does not invalidate Hajj.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that sa'y is a rukn. What is his evidence?
He cites the hadith: 'Allah has prescribed (kataba) sa'y upon you, so perform sa'y.'
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses Quran 2:158 ('no blame') which indicates permission, negating rukn status. Additionally, the word 'kataba' can be interpreted as recommendation (like in Quran 2:180).
Hanafis also argue that a rukn requires a decisive (qat'i) proof, which is absent here.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two rulings?
If sa'y is omitted: Hanafi = Hajj valid + dam required; Shafi'i = Hajj invalid, must be repeated.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why does the Hanafi view prevail?
The Quranic evidence is qat'i al-thubut and its permissive wording explicitly negates pillar status, while the Shafi'i proof is subject to interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَيَطُوفُ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطَ يَبْدَأُ بِالصَّفَا وَيَخْتِمُ بِالْمَرْوَةِ وَيَسْعَى فِي بَطْنِ الْوَادِي فِي كُلِّ شَوْطٍ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَإِنَّمَا يَبْدَأُ بِالصَّفَا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِيهِ إِبْدَوُا بِمَا بَدَاَ اللهُ تَعَالَى بِهِ ثُمَّ السَّعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ وَاجِبُ وَلَيْسَ بِرُكن و قَالَ الشَّافِعِي إِنَّهُ رُكُنَّ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ إِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ السَّعَى فَاسْعَوْا وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى ﴿فَلَا جُنَّاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ تَطَوَّفَ بِهِمَا ، وَمِثْلُهُ يُسْتَعْمَلُ لِلإِبَاحَةِ فَيَنْفِى الرُّكْنِيَّةَ وَالْإِيجَابُ إِلَّا إِنَّا عَدَلْنَا عَنْهُ فِي الْإِيجَابِ وَلِأَنَّ الرُّكْنَيَّةَ لَا تَنْبُتُ الإِبِدَلِيل مَقْطُوع بِهِ وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ ثُمَّ مَعْنَى مَا رَوَى كَتَبَ اسْتِحْبَابًا كَمَا فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ الآية
Then he makes seven circuits, beginning with al-Safa and ending with al-Marwah, and he runs in the valley in every circuit, due to what we have narrated. He begins with al-Safa because of his (saw) saying: 'Begin with what Allah began with.' Then sa'y between al-Safa and al-Marwah is wajib, not a rukn. Al-Shafi'i said it is a rukn because of his (saw) saying: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed sa'y upon you, so perform sa'y.' Our evidence is the saying of Allah: 'There is no blame upon him if he makes tawaf between them' (2:158). Such wording is used for permission, negating rukniyyah (pillar status) and obligation [in that context], except that we depart from it regarding obligation. And because rukniyyah cannot be established by a proof that is not decisive (qat'i), and none exists. Then the meaning of what he narrated ('prescribed') is as recommendation, like His saying: 'Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you...' (2:180).
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from al-Hidayah resolves the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on the legal status of sa'y. The matn states sa'y is wajib (obligatory) but not a rukn (pillar). Imam al-Shafi'i argues it is a rukn based on the hadith 'Allah has prescribed sa'y upon you, so perform sa'y'—the word 'prescribed' (kataba) implying obligation as a pillar. The Hanafi response: The Quranic verse (2:158) uses 'no blame', which typically indicates permissibility, not obligation. This wording would negate both pillar and obligation. However, Hanafis still consider sa'y wajib through other evidence (ijma and prophetic practice), but it does not rise to the level of rukn because a rukn requires a qat'i (definitive) proof. The hadith used by Shafi'i is interpreted as recommendation (istihbab), not decisive obligation, analogous to the verse about bequest (2:180) where 'prescribed' indicates recommendation. Therefore, sa'y is wajib—omission requires sacrifice (dam) but does not invalidate Hajj.

Key Terms
رُكن (Rukn): A pillar of an act of worship; omission invalidates the act entirely.
واجب (Wajib): An obligatory element whose omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the act.
كُتب (Kutiba): To prescribe or ordain; in the Shafi'i hadith, it is interpreted as obligation; Hanafis see it as recommendation in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of omitting sa'y according to the Hanafi school?
A) Hajj is invalid and must be repeated
B) Hajj remains valid but a dam (sacrifice) is required
C) No consequence, it is optional
D) Expiation equivalent to fasting three days

Key Takeaway
Sa'y is wajib in the Hanafi school: its omission requires a dam but does not invalidate Hajj.

The Actions of Sa'y: Walking and Running Between Safa and Marwah
Describes the sunnah actions of sa'y with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions of sa'y between Safa and Marwah and identify the hadith proof that establishes them.

Core Idea
Sa'y requires calm walking except in the valley where one runs; these actions are sunnah based on the Prophet's practice.

This lesson examines the specific actions of sa'y as described in the Hanafi matn and supported by hadith. You will learn the sequence of walking and running and understand the evidentiary basis for these acts, which are considered sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its description
The matn describes the steps: descend from Safa, walk calmly, run in the valley between the two green markers, then walk calmly again, ascend Marwah, and do as on Safa.
These are the recommended (sunnah) actions.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) narrated by multiple Companions, describing his own actions during sa'y.
The hadith is quoted in the matn: 'He descended from Safa... performed seven circuits.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly shows the Prophet's actions: descending, walking, running, walking, ascending. This becomes the model for the sunnah. The phrase 'this is one circuit' defines the unit of sa'y.
The Hanafi principle is that the Prophet's actions indicate sunnah unless accompanied by a command indicating obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Tahawi differed on the definition of a shawt, but the relied-upon view is that one shawt is from Safa to Marwah only.
This dispute does not affect the sunnah actions themselves.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hidayah's view is preferred due to the consensus of Companions that the Prophet performed seven circuits (seven crossings, not fourteen).
Thus the sunnah actions stand as described.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
سے نکلنے کو سنت کہتے ہیں۔
مروہ پر کیا اعمال کرے ، میلین اخضرین کے درمیان دوڑنے کا حکم
کتاب الحج
قَالَ ثُمَّ يَنْحِطُ نَحوَ الْمَرْوَةِ وَ يَمْشِي عَلى هَيْئَتِهِ فَإِذَا بَلَغَ بَطْنَ الْوَادِى يَسْعَى بَيْنَ الْمَيْلَيْنِ الْأَخْضَرَيْنِ سَعيًا ثُمَّ يَمْشِي عَلى هَيْئَتِهِ حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ الْمَرْوَةَ وَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا وَيَفْعَلُ كَمَا فَعَلَ عَلَى الصَّفَا لِمَارُوى أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَزَلَ مِنَ الصَّفَا وَجَعَلَ يَمْشِي نَحْوَ الْمَرْوَةِ وَسَعَى فِي بَطْنِ الْوَادِى حَتَّى إِذَا خَرَجَ مِنْ بَطْنِ الْوَادِى مَشَى حَتَّى صَعِدَ الْمَرْوَةَ وَطَافَ بَيْنَهُمَا سُبعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ وَهَذَا شَوطُ وَاحِدٌ
ترجمہ: قدوری نے کہا کہ پھر مروہ کی جانب اتر کر سکون کے ساتھ پر وقار انداز میں چلے پھرے جب بطن وادی میں پہنچے تو دونوں سبز میلین کے درمیان تھوڑا سا دوڑے۔ پھر سکون کے ساتھ پر وقار طریقہ سے چلے، یہاں تک کہ مروہ پر آ جائے اور اس پر چڑھے اور کرے جیسا کہ صفا پر کیا تھا۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم صفا سے اترے اور مروہ کی طرف چلنے لگے ۔ اور بطن وادی میں سعی کی یہاں تک کہ جب بطن وادی سے نکلے تو چلے یہاں تک کہ مروہ پر چڑھے اور ان دونوں کے درمیان سات پھیرے (چکر لگائے)۔ اور یہ ایک شوط ہے۔
تشریح: امام قدوری نے فرمایا کہ صفا سے مروہ کی طرف اترے اور انتہائی سکون اور وقار کے ساتھ چلے۔ پس جب بطن وادی میں پہنچے تو میلین اخضرین کے درمیان سعی کرے۔ پھر سکون کے ساتھ چل کر مروہ پر آجائے اور اس پر چڑھ جائے اور جو کام اس نے صفا پر کیا تھا وہی مروہ پر کرے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے جس کو صاحب ہدایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ صفا سے چل کر مروہ پر جانا ایک شوط ہے اور مروہ سے صفا کی طرف لوٹ کر آنا دوسرا شوط ہے۔ امام طحاوی نے فرمایا ہے کہ صفا سے مروہ پر جانا اور مروہ سے صفا کی طرف لوٹ کر آنا یہ ایک شوط ہے۔ لیکن اصح قول وہ ہے جس کو صاحب ہدایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے افعال حج کو روایت کرنے والے تمام حضرات صحابہ کا اس پر اتفاق ہے کہ آپ نے صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سات چکر لگائے ۔ اور امام طحاوی کے بیان کے مطابق بجائے سات کے چودہ شوط ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اس لئے صاحب ہدایہ کا بیان کردہ قول ہی اصح معلوم ہوتا ہے۔
The author said: Then he descends towards Marwah and walks in his normal manner. When he reaches the bottom of the valley, he runs quickly between the two green markers. Then he walks in his normal manner until he reaches Marwah and ascends upon it, and does as he did on Safa, due to the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) descended from Safa and began walking towards Marwah, and ran in the bottom of the valley until when he came out of the bottom of the valley, he walked until he ascended Marwah, and he performed seven circuits between them, and this is one circuit. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Then he descends towards Marwah and walks calmly and dignifiedly. When he reaches the bottom of the valley, he runs a little between the two green markers. Then he walks calmly and dignifiedly until he comes to Marwah and ascends upon it, and does as he did on Safa. Because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) descended from Safa and walked towards Marwah, and ran in the bottom of the valley until when he came out of the bottom of the valley, he walked until he ascended Marwah, and performed seven circuits between them, and this is one circuit. Commentary: Imam Quduri said: He descends from Safa towards Marwah and walks with utmost calm and dignity. When he reaches the bottom of the valley, he runs between the two green markers. Then he walks calmly until he reaches Marwah and ascends upon it, and does on Marwah what he did on Safa. The proof is this hadith which the author of Hidayah mentioned. The author of Hidayah said: Going from Safa to Marwah is one circuit, and returning from Marwah to Safa is a second circuit. Imam Tahawi said: Going from Safa to Marwah and returning from Marwah to Safa is one circuit. But the more correct statement is the one mentioned by the author of Hidayah, because all the Companions who narrated the actions of the Prophet during Hajj agree that he performed seven circuits between Safa and Marwah. According to Imam Tahawi's statement, there would be fourteen circuits instead of seven. Therefore, the statement of the author of Hidayah appears to be more correct.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof describing the manner of performing sa'y between Safa and Marwah. The author first states the ruling from the matn: after descending from Safa, one walks calmly until reaching the valley (Batan al-Wadi), where one runs between the two green markers. Then one resumes walking calmly until Marwah, ascends it, and repeats the same actions as on Safa. This is based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentary then explains that one circuit (shawt) is defined by the Hidayah as going from Safa to Marwah, while Imam Tahawi considers the round trip as one circuit. The Hidayah's view is preferred due to the consensus of the Companions that the Prophet performed seven circuits, not fourteen. The passage thus establishes the sunnah actions of sa'y and clarifies the definition of a circuit.

Key Terms
شوط (shawṭ): In this passage, one circuit of sa'y from Safa to Marwah (as per the relied-upon Hanafi position).
سعی (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah during Hajj or Umrah, consisting of running in the valley and walking elsewhere.
میلین اخضرین (al-mīlayn al-akhḍarayn): The two green markers in the valley between Safa and Marwah that define the area where one runs during sa'y.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Walk slowly.
B) Run quickly.
C) Stop and make du'a.
D) Walk backwards.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah actions of sa'y involve calm walking except in the valley where one runs, based on the Prophet's practice and the consensus of Companions on seven circuits.

The Definition of a Shawt in Sa'y: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Analyses the intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of a shawt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between the Hidayah and Imam Tahawi on the definition of one shawt in sa'y and state the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
One shawt is from Safa to Marwah; the round-trip view would double the circuits.

This lesson focuses on a specific point of difference within the Hanafi school: what constitutes one circuit (shawt) of sa'y. The Hidayah's view is that one shawt is a single crossing, while Imam Tahawi considered the round trip as one. Understanding this dispute clarifies the counting of the seven required circuits and ensures correct practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The relied-upon view is that one shawt equals going from Safa to Marwah.
This is the view of the Hidayah and the majority.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Tahawi (a Hanafi scholar) held that one shawt includes the round trip (Safa-Marwah-Safa).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Tahawi may have inferred from the continuous nature of sa'y that returning to Safa completes a cycle.
His reasoning is not quoted in detail here.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The response is based on the consensus of Companions that the Prophet performed seven circuits. If a round trip were one circuit, that would be fourteen crossings, contradicting the narrated number.
Thus the number of circuits is preserved as seven, not fourteen.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, the counting method differs. Both views cover the same total distance but differ in how many shawts are counted.
The mufta bihi is the Hidayah view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مروہ پر کیا اعمال کرے ، میلین اخضرین کے درمیان دوڑنے کا حکم

The Ruling of Sa'y: Wajib vs Rukn and Beginning with Safa
Inter-madhhab dispute on the ruling of sa'y: wajib vs rukn, and proof of beginning with Safa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that sa'y between Safa and Marwah is wajib not rukn, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument by analysing the dalil from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Sa'y is wajib, not rukn — omission requires compensation but does not invalidate Hajj.

In this passage, the Hanafi school defends its position that sa'y between Safa and Marwah is obligatory (wajib) but not a pillar (rukn). This distinction has real consequences: missing a rukn invalidates the Hajj, while missing a wajib only requires a sacrificial offering. The passage presents the Hanafi proof from the Quran and the Shafi'i opposing view from hadith, then resolves the apparent conflict through the principles of usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds sa'y to be wajib, not rukn. Note the practical implication: omission requires dam, not invalidation.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that al-Shafi'i (and Maliki, Hanbali) consider sa'y a rukn. Their evidence is the hadith: 'Allah has written sa'y upon you, so perform sa'y.'
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the word 'kataba' (written/prescribed) and the imperative 'fas'aw' imply obligation at the level of rukn.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi refutation: (1) Quran 2:158 'la junah' indicates permissibility, negating rukn; (2) the hadith is khabar wahid, insufficient for rukn; (3) the hadith is interpreted as recommendation (istihbab), like the bequest verse. Yet Hanafis affirm wujub due to other indicators.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if sa'y is omitted, Hanafi requires dam; Shafi'i requires repeating the Hajj/Umrah. This highlights the importance of the legal classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَيَطُوفُ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطَ يَبْدَأُ بِالصَّفَا وَيَخْتِمُ بِالْمَرْوَةِ وَيَسْعَى فِي بَطْنِ الْوَادِي فِي كُلِّ شَوْطٍ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَإِنَّمَا يَبْدَأُ بِالصَّفَا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِيهِ إِبْدَوُا بِمَا بَدَاَ اللهُ تَعَالَى بِهِ ثُمَّ السَّعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ وَاجِبُ وَلَيْسَ بِرُكن و قَالَ الشَّافِعِي إِنَّهُ رُكُنَّ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ إِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ السَّعَى فَاسْعَوْا وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى ﴿فَلَا جُنَّاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ تَطَوَّفَ بِهِمَا﴾ وَمِثْلُهُ يُسْتَعْمَلُ لِلإِبَاحَةِ فَيَنْفِى الرُّكْنِيَّةَ وَالْإِيجَابَ إِلَّا إِنَّا عَدَلْنَا عَنْهُ فِي الْإِيجَابِ وَلِأَنَّ الرُّكْنِيَّةَ لَا تَثْبُتُ إِلَّا بِدَلِيلٍ مَقْطُوعٍ بِهِ وَلَمْ يُوجَدْ ثُمَّ مَعْنَى مَا رَوَى كَتَبَ اسْتِحْبَابًا كَمَا فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ﴿كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ﴾ الآية
جمعہ: پس سات شوط طواف کرے۔ شروع کرے صفا سے اور ختم کرے مروہ پر اور ہر شوط میں بطن وادی میں سعی کرے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم روایت کر چکے۔ اور صفا سے اس لئے شروع کرے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ تم شروع کرو جس سے اللہ نے شروع کیا ہے۔

کتاب الحج
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
ہے۔ پھر صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرنا واجب ہے اور رکن نہیں ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ یہ سعی رکن ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تم پر سعی کرنا لکھ دیا ہے پس تم سعی کرو اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حج یا عمرہ کرنے والے پر کچھ گناہ نہیں ہے کہ وہ صفا اور مروہ کا طواف کرے۔ اور اس طرح کا کلام اباحت کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ پس رکنیت اور ایجاب دونوں منفی ہو جائیں گے مگر ہم نے ایجاب میں اس سے عدول کیا اور اس لئے کہ رکنیت ثابت نہیں ہوگی مگر دلیل قطعی ہے۔ حالانکہ ایسی دلیل نہیں پائی گئی ۔ پھر اس حدیث کے معنی جو امام شافعی نے روایت کی ہے۔ یہ ہے کہ مستحب ہونا لکھ دیا ہے جیسے کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول ﴿كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ﴾ الآية (البقرة:۱۸۰) میں ہے۔ تشریح: صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ طواف سات شوط (پھیرے) ہے، طواف کا آغاز صفا سے ہوگا اور اختتام مروہ پر ہوگا۔ اور ہر شوط میں بطن وادی میں سعی کرے گا۔ دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو گذشتہ مسئلہ کے ذیل میں گذر چکی ہے ۔ یعنی أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَزَلَ مِنَ الصَّفَا وَ جَعَلَ يَمْشِي نَحْوَ الْمَرْوَةِ الحديث ۔ اور صفا سے سعی کا آغاز کرنے پر یہ حدیث دلیل ہے إِبْدَوا بِمَا بَدَأَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى بِهِ یعنی جہاں سے اللہ نے ابتدا کی ہے تم بھی وہیں سے ابتداء کرو اور اللہ نے صفا سے ابتداء کی ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد ہے ﴿إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ الله﴾ (البقرة: ۱۵۸) اس حدیث میں لفظ ابدوا بصیغہ امر ہے۔ اس لئے ابتداء بالصفا واجب ہوگی۔ رہی یہ بات کہ صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرنا واجب ہے یا رکن ہے تو اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ ہمارے نزدیک رکن نہیں ہے بلکہ واجب ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک رکن ہے۔ یہی امام مالک اور امام احمد کا قول ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ﴿إِنَّ الله تعالى كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ السَّعَى فَاسْعَوا﴾ یعنی اللہ نے تم پر سعی کرنا لکھ دیا ہے تو تم سعی کرو اور لکھ دینا فرض اور رکن میں مستعمل ہے۔ اس لئے سعی کرنا رکن ہوگا۔ اور ہماری دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول ﴿فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا﴾ (البقرة: ۱۵۸) ہے۔ اس آیت سے استدلال اس طور پر ہوگا کہ لفظ لا جناح کا استعمال اباحت کے لئے ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول ﴿وَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِيمَا عَرَضْتُم به من خطبة النساء﴾ میں اباحت ہی مقصود ہے۔ کیونکہ معتدہ متوفی کو پیغام نکاح کا اشارہ کنایہ کرنا مباح ہے واجب یا فرض نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال لا جناح اباحت پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور جو لفظ اباحت کے لئے مستعمل ہو وہ رکن اور ایجاب کی نفی کر دیتا ہے تو بظاہر آیت سے یہ ثابت ہوا کہ سعی بین الصفا والمروہ نہ رکن ہے اور نہ واجب ہے۔ لیکن ایجاب کے حق میں ہم نے ظاہر آیت سے عدول کر لیا یعنی نفی ایجاب میں ظاہر آیت پر عمل کو ترک کر دیا۔ یعنی ظاہر آیت تو اس پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ سعی بین الصفا والمروہ واجب بھی نہ ہو مگر ہم نے اس پر عمل کرنے کو ترک کر دیا ہے۔ ایجاب کی نفی کے سلسلہ میں ظاہر آیت سے عدول اس لئے کیا گیا کہ حدیث ﴿إِنَّ اللهَ كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ السَّعَى فَاسْعَوْا﴾ خبر واحد ہے۔ اور خبر واحد وجوب پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس آیت کا اول ہے ﴿إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللَّهِ﴾ اور شعائر، شعیرۃ کی جمع ہے۔ اور شعیرۃ علامت کو کہتے ہیں۔ اور علامت دین فرض ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے آیت کا یہ حصہ سعی کے فرض ہونے پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ اور اس آیت کا آخری حصہ ﴿لَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا﴾ (البقرة:۱۵۸) سعی کے مباح ہونے پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ پس ہم نے دونوں پر عمل کیا۔ اور وجوب کے قائل ہو گئے۔ اس لئے کہ واجب عملاً اور اعتقاداً فرض نہیں ہوتا البتہ عملاً فرض ہوتا ہے۔ تیسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ ایجاب کی نفی پر عمل کرنے کو اجماع کی وجہ سے ترک کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ سعی بین الصفا والمروہ کے مباح ہونے کا کوئی قائل نہیں ہے۔ سعی کے واجب ہونے اور رکن نہ ہونے پر ہماری طرف سے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رکن ہونا دلیل قطعی سے ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ اور دلیل
He performs seven circuits, beginning at Safa and ending at Marwah, and he runs in the bottom of the valley in every circuit, due to what we have narrated. He begins at Safa because of the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement: 'Begin with what Allah began.' Then sa'y between Safa and Marwah is wajib, not rukn. Al-Shafi'i said it is rukn because of the Prophet's statement: 'Allah has written (prescribed) sa'y upon you, so perform sa'y.' Our proof is the saying of Allah: 'There is no sin upon him if he makes tawaf (sa'y) between them.' Such phrasing is used for permissibility (ibahah), so it negates rukniyyah and obligation, except that we have deviated from it regarding obligation. And because rukniyyah is not established except by a definitive proof, and such is not found. Moreover, the meaning of what he narrated (the hadith) is that it is written as recommended (istihbab), as in Allah's saying: 'Prescribed for you when death approaches one of you...' (Quran 2:180).
Translation/commentary: He performs seven circuits, beginning at Safa and ending at Marwah, and he runs in the bottom of the valley in every circuit, due to the hadith we narrated. He begins at Safa because the Prophet said: 'Begin with what Allah began.' Then sa'y between Safa and Marwah is wajib, not rukn. Al-Shafi'i said it is rukn because the Prophet said: 'Allah has written sa'y upon you, so perform sa'y.' Our proof is the verse: 'There is no sin upon him if he makes tawaf (sa'y) between them.' Such wording is used for permissibility, so it negates rukniyyah and obligation, but we have deviated from the apparent meaning regarding obligation. Rukniyyah is not established except by a definitive proof, and such is not found. Then the meaning of the hadith is that it is written as recommended, as in the verse about bequest. The commentary continues: Al-Quduri said: He performs seven circuits, beginning at Safa, ending at Marwah, and in every circuit he runs in the valley. The proof is the hadith mentioned earlier. Beginning at Safa is proven by the hadith: 'Begin with what Allah began,' and Allah began with Safa as in the verse: 'Indeed Safa and Marwah are among the symbols of Allah.' The word 'ibda'u' is imperative, so beginning with Safa is wajib. The dispute about sa'y being wajib or rukn: in our school it is wajib, not rukn; al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad say it is rukn. Al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith. Our proof is the verse 'there is no sin', which indicates permissibility and thus negates rukniyyah and obligation. However, we deviate from the apparent meaning regarding obligation due to several reasons: (1) The hadith is khabar wahid which indicates obligation. (2) The first part of the verse ('Indeed Safa and Marwah are among the symbols of Allah') indicates that sa'y is a symbol, and a symbol of the religion is obligatory. (3) There is consensus (ijma) that sa'y is not merely permissible; no one holds it to be merely permissible. So we affirm obligation (wajib) but not rukniyyah because rukniyyah requires a definitive proof, which is absent.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the legal status of sa'y between Safa and Marwah. The matn states that sa'y is wajib (obligatory) but not rukn (pillar). Imam al-Shafi'i argues it is rukn based on the hadith: 'Allah has written (prescribed) sa'y upon you, so perform sa'y.' The Hanafi response is based on the Quranic verse: 'There is no sin upon him if he makes tawaf (sa'y) between them' (2:158). The phrase 'la junah' (no sin) is used for permissibility, which negates both rukniyyah and obligation (wujub). However, the Hanafis deviate from this apparent meaning regarding obligation (they affirm wujub) due to three reasons: (1) The hadith cited by Shafi'i is khabar wahid, which indicates obligation. (2) The first part of the verse describes Safa and Marwah as 'sha'air Allah' (symbols of Allah), and symbols are obligatory. (3) There is consensus (ijma) that sa'y is not merely permissible; no one holds it to be merely mubah. So the Hanafis combine both proofs: they affirm wujub (obligation) but not rukniyyah, because rukniyyah requires a definitive (qat'i) proof, and the Quranic verse's apparent meaning of permissibility prevents the hadith from reaching that level. The passage also establishes that beginning sa'y at Safa is wajib based on the Prophet's command 'ibda'u bima bada'a Allah' (Begin with what Allah began), which is imperative. This is a ruling with proof and a well-structured legal argument.

Key Terms
واجب (wājib): Obligatory but not a pillar; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the Hajj/Umrah. In Hanafi usul, wajib is proven by zanni dalil, while fard is proven by qat'i dalil.
ركن (rukn): A pillar of Hajj/Umrah; if omitted, the act is invalid and must be repeated. In Hanafi usul, rukn requires definitive proof (qat'i thubut/dalalah).
شعائر (sha'ā'ir): Symbols or rites of Islam; here referring to Safa and Marwah as physical symbols that mark acts of worship. The term implies a degree of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school in this passage, what is the ruling of sa'y between Safa and Marwah?
A) Rukn (pillar) - omission invalidates Hajj.
B) Wajib (obligatory) - omission requires a dam but does not invalidate Hajj.
C) Sunnah (recommended) - no penalty for omission.
D) Mubah (permissible) - optional act.

Key Takeaway
Sa'y is wajib in the Hanafi school: obligatory but not a pillar; omission requires a sacrificial offering but does not invalidate the Hajj or Umrah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Sa'i Between Safa and Marwah: Wajib Not Rukn
Explains Hanafi position that Sa'i is wajib and refutes Shafi'i view that it is rukn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that Sa'i is wajib not rukn, identify the proofs from Quran and hadith, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Sa'i is wajib, not rukn: permissibility is overridden by command and consensus.

This passage addresses a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the status of Sa'i between Safa and Marwah. The Hanafi school holds it is wajib—obligatory but not a pillar—while the Shafi'i school considers it a rukn. Understanding this difference is crucial for knowing the consequences of omitting Sa'i during Hajj or Umrah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
State exactly what the Hanafi school holds: Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is wajib (obligatory) but not a rukn (pillar).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Identify Imam Shafi'i (and also Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad) who consider Sa'i a rukn.
The opposing school is the Shafi'i school primarily.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the opponent's main proof: the hadith 'Indeed Allah has written upon you Sa'i, so perform Sa'i' – they argue 'kutiba' indicates obligation and thus rukn.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: (1) 'kutiba' can mean recommended, as in the will verse; (2) rukn requires definitive proof, but this hadith is khabar wahid (zanni); (3) other evidences (sha'air, ijma) combine to establish wujub.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, omitting Sa'i requires dam (expiation) but the Hajj remains valid; in the Shafi'i school, the Hajj would be invalid if Sa'i is omitted intentionally.

کتاب الحج

اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
ہے۔ پھر صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرنا واجب ہے اور رکن نہیں ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ یہ سمعی رکن ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تم پر سعی کرنا لکھ دیا ہے پس تم سعی کرو اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حج یا عمرہ کرنے والے پر کچھ گناہ نہیں ہے کہ وہ صفا اور مروہ کا طواف کرے۔ اور اس طرح کا کلام اباحت کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ پس رکنیت اور ایجاب دونوں منفی ہو جائیں گے مگر ہم نے ایجاب میں اس سے عدول کیا اور اس لئے کہ رکنیت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ مگر دلیل قطعی ہے۔ حالانکہ ایسی دلیل نہیں پائی گئی ۔ پھر اس حدیث کے معنی جو امام شافعی نے روایت کی ہے۔ یہ ہے کہ مستحب ہونا لکھ دیا ہے جیسے کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ الآية (البقرة :۱۸۰) میں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ طواف سات شوط ( پھیرے) ہے، طواف کا آغاز صفا سے ہوگا اور اختتام مردہ پر ہوگا۔ اور ہر شوط میں بطن وادی میں سعی کرے گا۔ دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو گذشتہ مسئلہ کے ذیل میں گذر چکی ہے ۔ یعنی أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَزَلَ مِنَ الصَّفَا وَ جَعَلَ يَمْشِي نَحْوَ الْمَرْوَةِ الحديث ۔ اور صفا سے سعی کا آغاز کرنے پر یہ حدیث دلیل ہے إِبْدَوا بِمَا بَدَأَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى بِهِ یعنی جہاں سے اللہ نے ابتدا کی ہے تم بھی وہیں سے ابتداء صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرنا واجب ہے یا رکن ہے تو اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ ہمارے نزدیک رکن نہیں ہے بلکہ واجب ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک رکن ہے۔ یہی امام مالک اور امام احمد کا قول ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے إِنَّ الله تعالى كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ السَّعَى فَاسْعَوا یعنی اللہ نے تم پر سعی کرنا لکھ دیا ہے تو سو تم سعی کرو اور لکھ دینا فرض اور رکن میں مستعمل ہے۔ اس لئے سعی کرنار کن ہوگا۔ اور ہماری دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَلاَ جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا (البقرة: ۱۵۸) ہے۔ اس آیت سے استدلال اس طور پر ہوگا کہ لفظ لا جناح کا استعمال اباحت کے لئے ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِيمَا عَرَضْتُمْ به من خطبة النساء میں اباحت ہی مقصود ہے۔ کیونکہ معتدہ متوفی کو پیغام نکاح کا اشارہ کنایہ کرنا مباح ہے واجب یا فرض نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال لا جناح اباحت پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور جو لفظ اباحت کے لئے مستعمل ہو وہ رکن اور ایجاب کی نفی کر دیتا ہے تو بظاہر آیت سے یہ ثابت ہوا کہ سعی بین الصفا والمروہ نہ رکن ہے اور نہ واجب ہے۔ لیکن ایجاب کے حق میں ہم نے ظاہر آیت سے عدول کر لیا یعنی نفی ایجاب میں ظاہر آیت پر عمل کو ترک کر دیا۔ یعنی ظاہر آیت تو اس پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ سعی بین الصفاء المروہ واجب بھی نہ ہو مگر ہم نے اس پر عمل کرنے کو ترک کر دیا ہے۔ ایجاب کی نفی کے سلسلہ میں ظاہر آیت سے عدول اس لئے کیا گیا کہ حدیث انَّ اللهَ كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ السَّعَى فَاسْعَوْا خبر واحد ہے۔ اور خبر واحد وجوب پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس آیت کا اول ہے اِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللَّهِ اور شعائر ،شعیرۃ کی جمع ہے۔ اور شعیرۃ علامت کو کہتے ہیں۔ اور علامت دین فرض ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے آیت کا یہ حصہ سعی کے فرض ہونے پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ اور اس آیت کا آخری حصہ لَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُطْوَّفَ بِهِمَا (البقرة :۱۵۸) سعی کے مباح ہونے پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ پس ہم نے دونوں پر عمل کیا۔ اور وجوب کے قائل ہو گئے۔ اس لئے کہ واجب عملاً اور اعتقاداتو فرض نہیں ہوتا البتہ عملاً فرض ہوتا ہے۔ تیسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ ایجاب کی نفی پر عمل کرنے کو اجماع کی وجہ سے ترک کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ سعی بین الصفاء المروہ کے مباح ہونے کا کوئی قائل نہیں ہے۔ سعی کے واجب ہونے اور رکن نہ ہونے پر ہماری طرف سے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رکن ہونا دلیل قطعی سے ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ اور دلیل

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
۳۳۳
کتاب الحج قطعی پائی نہیں گئی۔ اس لئے سعی کارکن ہونا ثابت نہ ہو سکے گا۔ اور امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث إِنَّ اللهَ كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ السَّعَى فَاسْعَدا کا جواب یہ ہے کہ سعی کا مستحب ہونا لکھ دیا ہے۔ جیسا کہ دوسری آیت كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ میں ہے کہ موت کے وقت وصیت کرنا مستحب ہے نہ کہ فرض ۔ پس جس طرح یہاں لفظ كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ استحباب کے لئے ہے اسی طرح مسئلہ سعی میں بھی لفظ کتب استحباب یعنی غیر فرض کے لئے ہوگا۔
Then performing Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is wajib and not rukn. Imam Shafi'i said it is a rukn because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Allah has written upon you Sa'i, so perform Sa'i.' Our proof is that Allah said: 'There is no sin upon the one who performs Hajj or Umrah to circumambulate Safa and Marwah.' Such speech is used for ibaha (permissibility). Thus both rukn and obligation are negated, but we deviated from that in the case of obligation because rukn is not proven without a definitive proof, which is not found. Then the meaning of the hadith narrated by Imam Shafi'i is that it is mustahabb (recommended), like Allah's saying: 'Written upon you, when death approaches one of you...' (al-Baqarah 2:180). Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: Tawaf is seven circuits, beginning at Safa and ending at Marwah, and in each circuit he performs Sa'i in the valley. The proof is the hadith previously mentioned: 'The Prophet ﷺ descended from Safa and started walking towards Marwah.' And starting Sa'i from Safa is proven by the hadith: 'Start with what Allah began with' – Allah began with Safa, as He said: 'Indeed Safa and Marwah are from the symbols of Allah' (al-Baqarah 2:158). In this hadith, the word 'ibda' (start) is in the imperative form, so starting from Safa is wajib. As for whether Sa'i is wajib or rukn, there is disagreement. According to us, it is not rukn but wajib; according to Imam Shafi'i, it is rukn – this is also the view of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the hadith: 'Indeed Allah has written upon you Sa'i, so perform Sa'i' – and 'writing' is used for obligation and rukn. So Sa'i is rukn. Our proof is Allah's saying: 'So there is no sin upon him to circumambulate them' (al-Baqarah 2:158). The inference from this verse is that the phrase 'la junah' (no sin) is used for permission, as in Allah's saying: 'And there is no sin upon you concerning what you propose of marriage to women' – it indicates permission, not obligation or command. Thus 'la junah' indicates permissibility, and a word used for permissibility negates rukn and obligation. So apparently the verse proves that Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is neither rukn nor wajib. However, regarding obligation, we deviated from the apparent meaning, i.e., we abandoned acting upon the negation of obligation. That is, the apparent meaning indicates that Sa'i is not wajib, but we abandoned acting on that. The reason for deviating from the apparent meaning in the negation of obligation is the hadith 'Indeed Allah has written upon you Sa'i, so perform Sa'i' – it is a khabar wahid (solitary narration), and khabar wahid indicates obligation. The second reason is that the beginning of the verse is 'Indeed Safa and Marwah are from the symbols of Allah' – 'sha'air' (symbols) is plural of 'sha'irah', meaning sign, and the sign of a religion implies obligation. So this part of the verse indicates that Sa'i is obligatory. The latter part 'There is no sin upon him to circumambulate them' indicates permissibility. So we acted upon both and held it to be wajib, because wajib is practically obligatory but not obligatory in belief. The third reason is that we abandoned acting upon the negation of obligation due to consensus (ijma), as no one holds Sa'i to be merely permissible. Our second proof for Sa'i being wajib and not rukn is that rukn is proven by definitive evidence, and such evidence is not found. Therefore, Sa'i cannot be proven as rukn. As for the hadith presented by Imam Shafi'i, the response is that 'written' here means recommended, as in the other verse: 'Written upon you, when death approaches one of you...' where making a will at death is mustahabb, not fard. So just as 'kutiba alaykum' there indicates recommendation, similarly here it indicates recommendation, not obligation.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the legal status of Sa'i between Safa and Marwah. The Hanafi position is that Sa'i is wajib (obligatory) but not a rukn (pillar). Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad hold it to be a rukn. The author presents the proofs for both sides and explains the Hanafi reasoning. The Quranic verse (2:158) uses 'la junah' which typically indicates permissibility, which would negate obligation. However, the Hanafis combine this with other evidences: the hadith of the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) that 'Allah has written upon you Sa'i' (which indicates obligation via khabar wahid), the fact that Safa and Marwah are called 'sha'air Allah' (symbols of Allah) which implies their rites are obligatory, and the consensus (ijma) that Sa'i is not merely permissible but obligatory. The refutation of the Shafi'i hadith is that 'kutiba' (written) can mean recommended, as in the verse about wills. Thus, the Hanafi school concludes that Sa'i is wajib—practically obligatory but not a foundational pillar—and it is not a rukn because rukn requires definitive evidence (dalil qat'i), which is absent here.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah seven times during Hajj or Umrah.
رکن (rukn): A fundamental integral of Hajj/Umrah whose omission invalidates the act.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory element whose omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of Sa'i between Safa and Marwah, and what is required if it is omitted?
A) Rukn – Hajj is invalid without it.
B) Wajib – dam (expiation) is required if omitted.
C) Sunnah – no compensation needed.
D) Mubah – optional and no sin if left.

Key Takeaway
Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school; omitting it requires dam but does not invalidate the Hajj.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner

Staying in Makkah in Ihram After Sa'i: Voluntary Tawaf Without Repeating Sa'i
States ruling on voluntary tawaf and Sa'i after initial Sa'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing voluntary tawaf and Sa'i during the stay in Makkah after the initial Sa'i, and explain the dalil from hadith.

Core Idea
Sa'i is wajib only once; voluntary tawaf is sunnah but does not warrant a repeat of Sa'i.

After completing the initial Tawaf al-Qudum and Sa'i, the pilgrim remains in ihram until the rites of Hajj. This lesson explains what acts are permitted during that stay—voluntary tawaf is encouraged, but Sa'i is not repeated. The proof is the hadith that tawaf is like prayer, and prayer can be performed at any time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pilgrim's status
Recognize that after Sa'i, the pilgrim is still in ihram for Hajj and cannot become halal until completing the Hajj actions.
This is a fundamental principle: ihram remains until the acts of Hajj are done.
2
Determine the ruling on voluntary tawaf
The pilgrim may perform voluntary tawaf (nafl tawaf) as much as desired. The basis is the hadith that tawaf resembles prayer, which is a good deed that can be done at any time (except forbidden times).
The hadith: الطَّوَافُ بِالْبَيْتِ صَلوةٌ
3
Recognize the prohibition of repeating Sa'i
After these voluntary tawafs, Sa'i is not performed because Sa'i is wajib only once in Hajj (after Tawaf al-Qudum or the obligatory tawaf). Performing Sa'i as a voluntary act is not legislated in the Hanafi school.
This is a point of ikhtilaf: some Shafi'i scholars allow voluntary Sa'i.
4
Apply the sunnah of two rak'ahs after tawaf
After every seven circuits (shout) of tawaf, the pilgrim prays two rak'ahs, known as salat al-tawaf. This applies to both obligatory and voluntary tawaf.
These two rak'ahs are sunnah mu'akkadah.

Source Text

ثُمَّ يُقِيمُ بِمَكَّةَ حَرَامًا لِأَنَّهُ مُحْرِمُ بِالْحَجِّ فَلَا يَتَحَلَّلُ قَبْلَ الْإِثْيَانِ بِأَفْعَالِهِ وَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ كَمَا بَدَالَهُ لِأَنَّهُ يُشْبِهُ الصَّلوةَ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الطَّوَافُ بِالْبَيْتِ صَلوةُ وَالصَّلوةُ خَيْرٌ مَوضُوعِ فَكَذَا الطَّوَافُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا يَسْعَى عَقِيبَ هذِهِ الْأُطُوفَةِ فِي هَذِهِ الْمُدَّةِ لِأَنَّ السَّعْيَ لَا يَجِبُ فِيهِ إِلَّا مَرَّةَ وَالتَنْقُلُ بِالسَّعِى غَيْرُ مَشْرُوعِ وَيُصَلَّى لِكُلِّ أَسْبُوعِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَهِيَ رَكَعَنَا الطَّرَافِ عَلَى مَا بَيِّنا
ترجمہ پھر بحالت احرام مکہ المکرمہ میں ٹھہرا رہے۔ کیونکہ یہ شخص حج کا اجرام باندھنے والا ہے۔ اس لئے حج کے افعال ادا کرنے سے پہلے حلال نہیں ہوگا۔ اور جب جب اس کا جی چاہے بیت اللہ کا طواف کرتا رہے۔ کیونکہ طواف نماز کے مشابہ ہے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ بیت اللہ کا طواف کرنا نماز ہے اور نماز نیکی بنا کر وضع کی گئی ہے۔ پس اسی طرح طواف بھی ( خیر موضوع ہے ) مگر شخص اس مدت میں ان ( نفلی ) طوافوں کے بعد سعی نہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ حج میں سنی ایک ہی مرتبہ واجب ہوتی ہے اور نفلی طور پر سعی کرنا مشروع نہیں ہے او ریہ ہر سات چکر پر دو رکعت پڑھے۔ اور یہ طواف کی دورکعتیں ہیں ۔ اس بنیاد پر جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ طواف قدوم اور سعی سے فراغت کے بعد یہ شخص بحالت احرام مکتہ المکرمہ میں قیام کرے۔ کیونکہ اس نے حج ادا کرنے کے ارادہ سے احرام باندھا ہے۔ اس لئے بغیر افعال حج ادا کئے احرام سے نہ نکلے یعنی ایسا کوئی کام نہ کرے جس سے احرام سے باہر ہو جاتا ہے۔ البتہ اس مدت قیام میں جب جی چاہے طواف کرتا رہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طواف نماز کے مشابہ ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے الطَّوَافُ بِالْبَيْتِ صَلوةٌ إِلَّا أَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى اَحَلَّ فِيهِ الْمَنْطِقُ فَمَنْ نَطَقَ فِيهَ فَلَايَنْطِقُ إِلَّا بِخیر یعنی خانہ کعبہ کا طواف کرنا نماز ہے مگر اللہ تعالیٰ نے طواف کے اندر بات کرنا حلال کر دیا ہے۔ پس جو کوئی طواف کے اندر بات کرے تو نہ بولے مگر اچھی بات۔ اس حدیث سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ طواف نماز کے مشابہ ہے اور نماز ایک نیک کام ہے جس کو چند مخصوص اوقات کے علاوہ ہر وقت ادا کیا جا سکتا ہے پس اسی طرح طواف بھی ہر وقت کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ اس مدت میں ان نفلی طوافوں کے بعد صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی نہیں کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ سعی فقط ایک بار واجب ہے اور وہ طواف قدوم کے بعد کی جا چکی۔ اور رہا بطور نفل سعی کرنا تو وہ مشروع نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ایک سعی کے بعد دوبارہ بھی نہ کی جائے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ نیلی طواف کرنے والا ہر سات شوط پر دورکعت نماز پڑھے۔ اور یہ دو رکعت صلوۃ طواف کہلاتی ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں حدیث گذر چکی ہے۔
Then he stays in Makkah while in ihram, because he is in ihram for Hajj and cannot become halal before performing its actions. He performs tawaf around the House as much as he wishes, because tawaf resembles prayer. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Tawaf around the House is prayer, and prayer is the best of deeds, so tawaf is likewise.' However, he does not perform Sa'i after these tawafs during this period, because Sa'i is only wajib once, and performing Sa'i as nafl is not legislated. And he prays two rak'ahs for every seven circuits, and these are the two rak'ahs of tawaf, as we have explained. Translation: Then he stays in Makkah while in ihram. Because this person is in ihram for Hajj, he will not become halal before performing the acts of Hajj. Whenever he wishes, he may perform tawaf around the Ka'bah, because tawaf resembles prayer. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Tawaf around the House is prayer, except that Allah has permitted speech during it. So whoever speaks should only speak good.' This hadith shows that tawaf resembles prayer, and prayer is a good deed that can be performed at any time except specific times. Similarly, tawaf can be performed at any time. However, during this period, after these voluntary tawafs, he should not perform Sa'i between Safa and Marwah, because Sa'i is only wajib once, and it has already been performed after tawaf al-qudum. As for performing Sa'i as nafl, it is not legislated. Therefore, after one Sa'i, it should not be repeated. Sahib al-Hidayah says: The one performing these voluntary tawafs should pray two rak'ahs after every seven circuits, and these two rak'ahs are called salat al-tawaf, as the hadith has been mentioned previously.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the actions of a pilgrim after completing the initial Tawaf al-Qudum and Sa'i. The pilgrim, still in ihram, remains in Makkah until the rites of Hajj begin. During this stay, he may perform voluntary tawaf (nafl tawaf) around the Ka'bah as much as he wishes. This is based on the hadith that tawaf is like prayer, and prayer can be offered at any time except forbidden times. However, he should not perform Sa'i after these voluntary tawafs, because Sa'i is only obligatory once in Hajj (after Tawaf al-Qudum or the obligatory tawaf). Performing Sa'i as a voluntary act is not legislated in the Hanafi school. After each seven circuits of tawaf, he prays two rak'ahs, which are known as salat al-tawaf. This applies to both obligatory and voluntary tawaf. The text also explains that the pilgrim must remain in ihram and not do anything that would break it until the Hajj actions are completed. The commentary by Sahib al-Hidayah and Sahib al-Quduri reinforces these points.

Key Terms
طواف نفل (tawaf nafl): Voluntary circumambulation of the Ka'bah, performed at any time during the stay in Makkah.
سعي (sa'y): The ritual walking seven times between Safa and Marwah, wajib once in Hajj and Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is mustahabb to perform Sa'i after each tawaf.
B) It is wajib to perform Sa'i after each tawaf.
C) It is not permissible to perform Sa'i after voluntary tawaf.
D) It is permissible but not recommended.

Key Takeaway
Sa'i is wajib only once in Hajj; voluntary tawaf is allowed and rewarded, but Sa'i is not repeated after it.

The Obligation Status of Sa'y: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Response to Shafi'i's argument that sa'y is fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sa'y and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the analogy of the will verse.

Core Idea
Sa'y is not a pillar of Hajj—the word 'kataba' does not necessarily imply obligation.

The legal status of sa'y (walking between Safa and Marwa) is a point of contention between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This passage presents the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof that sa'y is fard (a pillar). By drawing an analogy with a Quranic verse about wills, the Hanafi school demonstrates that the word 'kataba' (prescribed) can indicate recommendation (istihbab) rather than obligation. Let's unpack this argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i cites a hadith: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed sa'y upon you, so perform sa'y.' The imperative and the word 'kataba' appear to show obligation.
2
Analyze the Hanafi objection
The Hanafi school argues that 'kataba' does not necessarily imply fard; it can mean mustahab. They support this with a parallel verse about wills (2:180).
The verse: كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ إِن تَرَكَ خَيْرًا الْوَصِيَّةُ (Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth, to make a will...). This is widely understood as mustahab, not fard.
3
Understand the qiyas
If the same expression yields mustahab in one context, it can do so in another. Thus, the hadith on sa'y indicates recommendation, not obligation.
4
Determine the practical consequence
If sa'y were fard, omitting it would invalidate Hajj. According to the Hanafi view here, omitting sa'y does not invalidate, though the standard Hanafi position is that it is wajib (requiring a dam).
thamarah al-khilaf

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج قطعی پائی نہیں گئی۔ اس لئے سعی کارکن ہونا ثابت نہ ہو سکے گا۔ اور امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث إِنَّ اللهَ كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ السَّعَى فَاسْعَدا کا جواب یہ ہے کہ سعی کا مستحب ہونا لکھ دیا ہے۔ جیسا کہ دوسری آیت كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ میں ہے کہ موت کے وقت وصیت کرنا مستحب ہے نہ کہ فرض ۔ پس جس طرح یہاں لفظ كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ استحباب کے لئے ہے اسی طرح مسئلہ سعی میں بھی لفظ کتب استحباب یعنی غیر فرض کے لئے ہوگا۔
The Book of Hajj: It was not found as definitive (qat'i). Therefore, sa'y cannot be proven to be a pillar (rukn). And the answer to the hadith presented by Imam Shafi'i, 'Indeed Allah has prescribed sa'y upon you, so perform sa'y,' is that it indicates the mustahab (recommended) nature of sa'y, just as in the other verse 'Prescribed upon you when death approaches one of you...' where making a will at death is mustahab, not fard. So just as the word 'kutiba alaykum' here indicates istihbab (recommendation), similarly in the issue of sa'y the word 'kutiba' will indicate istihbab, i.e., not fard.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the legal status of sa'y (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwa). The Hanafi position is that sa'y is not a fard (obligatory pillar) of Hajj. The author argues that Shafi'i's evidence—a hadith stating that Allah has prescribed sa'y (using the word kataba)—is not definitive (qat'i) in its indication. To support this, the author draws an analogy with a verse about wills: the same expression 'kutiba alaykum' is used, yet scholars agree that making a will at death is mustahab (recommended) and not fard. Therefore, the Hanafi response is that the word kataba in the context of sa'y similarly implies recommendation, not obligation. This is a classic Hanafi use of qiyas with a parallel text to clarify the intended meaning of a command.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): The ritual walking between the hills of Safa and Marwa during Hajj or Umrah.
مستحب (mustahab): In this passage, used to mean 'non-fard' (not a pillar), but in Hanafi usul it is a recommended act below sunnah. Here it is polemical.
فرض (fard): An obligatory act that is a pillar (rukn) of the act of worship; omission invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, which Quranic verse is used to argue that the word 'kataba' (prescribed) does not necessarily imply fard?
A) The verse on wills (2:180)
B) The verse on fasting (2:183)
C) The verse on prayer (2:110)
D) The verse on Hajj (3:97)

Key Takeaway
The word 'kataba' is ambiguous; the Hanafi school uses a Quranic parallel to show it can indicate recommendation, thus sa'y is not a pillar of Hajj.

Nafl Tawaf and Non-Repetition of Sa'y
Ruling with proof from Sunnah on nafl tawaf and non-repetition of sa'y.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl tawaf while in ihram and explain why sa'y cannot be repeated as a voluntary act.

Core Idea
Tawaf is like prayer: you may do it anytime, but sa'y is wajib only once.

After completing the initial tawaf al-qudum and sa'y, the pilgrim remains in ihram until the acts of Hajj are done. During this waiting period, the Hanafi school permits voluntary (nafl) tawaf at any time, citing a hadith that likens tawaf to prayer. However, sa'y is a unique obligation that cannot be repeated as a supererogatory act. This lesson unpacks the evidence and rulings behind these two distinct acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage discusses two acts: tawaf (circumambulation) and sa'y (walking between Safa and Marwa). Determine the ruling for each in this context: tawaf is permissible as nafl; sa'y is wajib only once and not to be repeated.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'Tawaf of the House is prayer.' Identify the type of proof (hadith ahad) and its source.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith analogizes tawaf to prayer. From this, the Hanafi school derives that tawaf, like prayer, can be performed at any time (except prohibited times) and has similar conditions of purity. It also implies that tawaf is a virtuous act that can be repeated.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on sa'y
Some scholars permit repeating sa'y voluntarily. The Hanafi school restricts it to once. Identify the practical consequence of this difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
The source states that nafl sa'y is 'ghayr mashru' (not legislated).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author relies on the positions of Al-Quduri and Al-Hidayah. The mufta bihi is that nafl tawaf is permissible but sa'y is wajib once only.
This is the established Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah).
