Commentary
This passage explains the manner of combining Zuhr and Asr on the Day of Arafah. The ruling is that the imam leads both prayers at the time of Zuhr with a single adhan and two iqamahs. The proof for combining is the widely transmitted practice (nagl mustafid). The proof for the specific method of one adhan and two iqamahs is from the hadith of Jabir. The rationale is that since Asr is offered before its usual time, and everyone is already gathered, only an iqamah is needed to signal the start of Asr, not another adhan.

Key Terms
جمع بین الصلاتین (jam' bayn al-salātayn): Combining Zuhr and Asr prayers on the Day of Arafah at the time of Zuhr.
نقل مستفیض (naql mustafid): A widely transmitted narration that is not as strong as mutawatir but is accepted due to widespread agreement.

Nafl Between Combined Prayers on Arafah and Adhan Repetition Dispute
Ruling on nafl between combined prayers and adhan repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl between Zuhr and Asr on Arafah and distinguish the positions of Zahir al-Riwayah and Imam Muhammad regarding the repetition of adhan.

Core Idea
Praying nafl between combined prayers on Arafah is makruh and, according to the relied-upon view, necessitates repeating the adhan.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific issue related to Hajj: the ruling on voluntary prayers (nafl) between the combined Zuhr and Asr on the Day of Arafah. While the primary ruling is that such nafl is disliked, a secondary dispute arises within the Hanafi school about whether doing so invalidates the adhan for Asr. Understanding this nuance highlights the importance of continuity in the adhan and the hierarchical authority within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing nafl prayer between the combined Zuhr and Asr on Arafah. The ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah is that it is makruh tanzih (disliked).
2
State the intra-Hanafi dispute
According to Zahir al-Riwayah (position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if nafl is performed, the adhan for Asr must be repeated. Imam Muhammad holds that the adhan remains valid and does not need repetition.
3
Analyze the dalil for Zahir al-Riwayah
The reasoning (talil) is that any intervening act (nafl or other work) cuts the connection (ittisal) of the first adhan, thus necessitating repetition.
The Arabic phrase 'يقطع فور الآذان الأول' is key.
4
Understand Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad considers the adhan still valid despite the interruption. His specific dalil is not detailed in this passage.
5
Apply the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is Zahir al-Riwayah, as taken by the author of al-Hidayah. The authority weight is 'zahir_riwayah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظہر اور عصر کے درمیان نفل پڑھنے کا حکم وَلَا يَتَطَوَّعُ بَيْنَ الصَّلوتَيْنِ تَحْصِيْلاً لِمَقْصُودِ الوُقُوفِ وَلِهَذَا قَدِمَ الْعَصْرُ على وقته فلو أنَّه فَعَلَ فَعَلَ مَكْرُوها وأعَادَ الْأَذَانَ لِلْعَصْرِ فِي طَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ خِلَاقًا لِمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّ الْاِشْتِغَالَ بِالتَّطَوَّعَ أَو بِعَمَلِ اخَرَ يَقْطَعُ فَوْرُ الْآذَانِ الْأَوَّلِ فَيُعِيدُهُ لِلْعَصْرِ : ترجمہ اور دونوں نمازوں کے درمیان نفل نہ پڑھے تا کہ وقوف عرفہ کا مقصود حاصل ہو جائے اور اسی وجہ سے عصر کو اس کے وقت پر مقدم کیا گیا۔ پس اگر اس نے یہ کیا تو مکروہ کام کیا۔ اور ظاہر الروایہ میں عصر کے لئے اذان کا اعادہ کرے۔ برخلاف اس کے جو امام محمد سے روایت کیا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ نفل یا دوسرے کام میں مشغول ہونا اذان اول کے اتصال کو ختم کر دیتا ہے اس لئے عصر کے لئے اس کا اعادہ کرے گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ، امام یا مقتدی دونوں نمازوں ظہر اور عصر کے درمیان نفل نماز نہ پڑھے یعنی فرض نماز کے علاوہ سنت وغیرہ کچھ نہ پڑھے ۔ کیونکہ آج کے دن وقوف عرفہ مقصود ہے۔ لہذا اس مقصود کو حاصل کرنے کے لئے اپنا وقت نفل وغیرہ دوسرے کاموں میں صرف نہ کرے۔ اسی مقصد کے پیش نظر عصر کی نماز اپنے وقت پر مقدم کر دی گئی ہے۔ لیکن اسکے باوجود اگر امام یا مقتدی نے دونوں نمازوں کے درمیان نفل نماز پڑھے تو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق عصر کے لئے اذان کا اعادہ کرے۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک اس صورت میں اذان کا اعادہ نہیں ہے۔ ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ظہر کی نماز کے بعد نفل یا دوسرے کام میں مشغول ہونا چونکہ عصر کے ساتھ اذان اول کے اتصال کو ختم کر دیتا ہے اس لئے عصر کے واسطے اذان کا اعادہ کیا جائے گا۔
Ruling on performing nafl between the two prayers: And he should not perform supererogatory prayer between the two prayers, in order to achieve the purpose of standing (wuquf), and for this reason Asr was advanced before its time. So if he does so, he does a disliked act, and he must repeat the adhan for Asr in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), contrary to what is narrated from Muhammad. Because occupying oneself with supererogatory prayer or another act cuts the connection of the first adhan, so he repeats it for Asr. Translation: And he should not pray nafl between the two prayers so that the purpose of standing at Arafah is achieved, and for this reason Asr was advanced to its time. So if he does this, he has done a disliked act. And in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), he should repeat the adhan for Asr, contrary to what is narrated from Imam Muhammad. Because engaging in nafl or other work breaks the connection of the first adhan, so he should repeat it for Asr. Commentary: Issue: The imam or the follower should not perform nafl prayer between the two prayers (Zuhr and Asr), meaning besides the obligatory prayer, he should not perform any sunnah etc. Because on this day, the standing at Arafah is the objective. Therefore, to achieve this objective, he should not spend his time in nafl or other activities. For this same purpose, the Asr prayer was advanced to its earlier time. Nevertheless, if the imam or follower does perform nafl prayers between the two prayers, then according to Zahir al-Riwayah, he should repeat the adhan for Asr. According to Imam Muhammad, he does not repeat the adhan. The evidence of Zahir al-Riwayah is that engaging in nafl or other work after Zuhr prayer breaks the connection of the first adhan with Asr, so he must repeat the adhan for Asr.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage prohibits performing any voluntary prayers (nafl) between the combined Zuhr and Asr prayers on the Day of Arafah. The purpose is to focus on the standing at Arafah. If someone violates this and prays nafl, it is makruh (disliked). Additionally, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the adhan for Asr must be repeated. According to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah, the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the adhan must be repeated because the interruption (praying or doing another act) severs the linkage of the original adhan to the Asr prayer. Imam Muhammad holds that the adhan does not need to be repeated. The relied-upon position is the one from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted narrations from the early Hanafi imams through Imam Muhammad's six books. This is the most authoritative layer in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Praying nafl between the combined prayers on Arafah is makruh, and according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, it necessitates repeating the adhan for Asr.

Combining Zuhr and 'Asr at Arafat with One Adhan and Two Iqamahs
Ruling on combining two prayers at Arafat with one adhan and two iqamahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for combining Zuhr and 'Asr at Arafat, explain the proof from the Sunnah, and identify the reason for one adhan and two iqamahs.

Core Idea
At Arafat, one adhan for both prayers but two iqamahs – because 'Asr is offered early, a separate iqamah alerts the people.

In Hajj, at the plain of Arafat, the imam combines Zuhr and 'Asr prayers with a unique call arrangement. This lesson examines the ruling that only one adhan is given for both prayers, followed by two separate iqamahs. Understanding this practice helps clarify the Hanafi position on the use of adhan and iqamah for combined prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the imam commanded to do? Combine Zuhr and 'Asr with one adhan and two iqamahs.
This is a sunnah muakkadah, not fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jabir (RA) where the Prophet (PBUH) did exactly this at Arafat.
This hadith is in Sahih Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's actual practice (fi'l) indicates that this is the recommended way. The specific elements (one adhan, two iqamahs) are transmitted.
Fi'l of the Prophet is a proof for sunnah.
4
Understand the 'illah (reason)
Why only one adhan? Because the congregation is already gathered from the first adhan. Why two iqamahs? To separately announce each prayer, especially 'Asr which is performed before its usual time.
The reason is educational: to inform the people that 'Asr is being offered early.
5
Note the authority weight
This ruling comes from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi. The hadith is ahad, so the hukm is sunnah, not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لِلظَّهْرِ ثُمَّ يُقِيمُ لِلْعَصْرِ لِأَنَّ الْعَصْرَ يَوَدُّى قَبْلَ وَقِتِهِ الْمَعْهُودِ فَيُفْرِدُ بِالْإِقَامَةِ إِعْلَامَا لِلنَّاسِ
For Zuhr, then he gives iqamah for 'Asr because 'Asr is performed before its usual time, so he singles it out with iqamah to inform the people.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that at Arafat, the imam combines Zuhr and 'Asr with one adhan and two iqamahs. The reason given is that 'Asr is offered before its usual time (i.e., in the time of Zuhr), so only an iqamah is needed to alert the people since they are already gathered from the adhan for Zuhr. This practice is based on the authentic hadith of Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) reported in Sahih Muslim, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed the two prayers at Arafat with one adhan and two iqamahs. The ruling is specific to the imam leading the congregation; the individual who prays alone has a separate ruling discussed elsewhere.

Key Terms
أَذَان (adhan): The call to prayer announcing the beginning of the time for the obligatory prayer.
إِقَامَة (iqamah): The second call immediately before the prayer begins, indicating the prayer is about to start.
جَمْع بَيْن الصَّلَاتَيْن (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two obligatory prayers at the time of one, specifically Zuhr and 'Asr at Arafat in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Two adhans and two iqamahs
B) One adhan and two iqamahs
C) One adhan and one iqamah
D) Two adhans and one iqamah

Key Takeaway
At Arafat, combining Zuhr and 'Asr requires one adhan and two iqamahs, based on the Prophet's practice.

Nafl Between Combined Prayers at Arafat and Adhan Repetition
Intra-Hanafi dispute on adhan repetition after nafl between combined prayers at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafl between Zuhr and 'Asr at Arafat and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on adhan repetition, citing the 'illa for the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Nafl between Zuhr and 'Asr at Arafat is makruh; engaging in it requires repeating the adhan for 'Asr according to Zahir al-Riwayah.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh texts addresses a specific rule for the Day of Arafat: no voluntary prayer (nafl) between the combined Zuhr and 'Asr prayers, to preserve focus on wuquf. It also reveals an intra-Hanafi disagreement: if one does perform nafl, must the adhan for 'Asr be repeated? We will examine the reasoning behind the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and its legal classification. The act is performing voluntary prayer (nafl) between the two combined prayers (Zuhr and 'Asr) at Arafat. The ruling is makruh (disliked).
2
Locate the 'illa for prohibition
Find the reason given for the prohibition. The text states: 'to achieve the purpose of standing (wuquf)'. Therefore, 'Asr was brought forward. The prohibition of nafl is to maintain focus on wuquf.
3
Identify the consequence if done
If one still performs nafl, the text says 'he has done something makruh' and then discusses the adhan. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, the adhan for 'Asr must be repeated. This is the relied-upon position.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that Imam Muhammad narrates a contrary view that repetition is not required. Understand the 'illa for the Zahir al-Riwayah position: engaging in nafl or other work cuts the continuity (fawr) of the first adhan, necessitating a repeat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَتَطَوَّعُ بَيْنَ الصَّلوتَيْنِ تَحْصِيْلاً لِمَقْصُودِ الوُقُوفِ وَلِهَذَا قَدِمَ الْعَصْرُ على وقته فلو أنَّه فَعَلَ فَعَلَ مَكْرُوها وأعَادَ الْأَذَانَ لِلْعَصْرِ فِي طَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ خِلَاقًا لِمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّ الْاِشْغَالَ بِالتَّطَوَّعَ أَو بِعَمَلِ اخَرَ يَقْطَعُ فَوْرُ الْآذَانِ الْأَوَّلِ فَيُعِيدُهُ لِلْعَصْرِ
And he should not perform voluntary prayer between the two prayers, to achieve the purpose of standing (wuquf). Therefore 'Asr was brought forward from its time. So if he did that, he has done something makruh. And he should repeat the adhan for 'Asr according to Zahir al-Riwayah, contrary to what has been narrated from Muhammad, because engaging in voluntary prayer or other work cuts the continuity of the first adhan, so he repeats it for 'Asr.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific ruling for the Day of Arafat: one should not engage in any voluntary prayer (nafl) between the two combined prayers (Zuhr and 'Asr). The reason is to fully dedicate oneself to the primary act of standing at Arafat (wuquf), which is the essence of Hajj. Because the focus is on wuquf, 'Asr is brought forward to the time of Zuhr. If a person nevertheless prays nafl between the two, it is considered makruh (disliked). The ruling then discusses the adhan: according to Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon transmission from the school), the adhan for 'Asr must be repeated, because the connection between the first adhan (for Zuhr) and the subsequent 'Asr prayer is broken by the intervening voluntary act. Imam Muhammad holds that repetition is not required. The reason for the Zahir al-Riwayah position is that the first adhan is linked to the subsequent prayer, and any interruption nullifies the continuity. Therefore, to maintain the proper sequence, a new adhan is given for 'Asr.

Key Terms
التَّطَوُّع (al-tatawwu'): Voluntary or supererogatory prayer (nafl) beyond the obligatory prayers.
ظَاهِر الرِّوَايَة (Zahir al-Riwayah): The most authoritative transmission of the Hanafi school, from the six core books of Imam Muhammad.
إِعَادَة الْأَذَان (i'adat al-adhan): Repeating the adhan for 'Asr after an interruption between the combined prayers.
فَوْر (fawr): Immediate continuity; the uninterrupted sequence between adhan and iqama or prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, if someone prays nafl between Zuhr and 'Asr at Arafat, what must be done?
A) Nothing, the prayer is valid without any change.
B) The nafl prayer must be repeated.
C) The adhan for 'Asr must be repeated.
D) The entire combination is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that nafl between combined prayers at Arafat is makruh and, if performed, necessitates repeating the adhan for 'Asr to restore continuity.

Khutbah at Arafat Is Not a Fard Requirement
Ruling that Arafat khutbah is not fard; prayer valid without it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the khutbah at Arafat is not fard and explain why its omission does not invalidate the combined prayer.

Core Idea
The Arafat khutbah is sunnah, not fard – omitting it does not affect the prayer's validity.

This lesson clarifies the status of the khutbah (sermon) delivered at Arafat before the combined prayer. Many assume it is a necessary condition like the Friday khutbah, but the Hanafi school teaches otherwise. By the end, you will be able to articulate the correct ruling and distinguish it from Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The imam praying the combined zuhr and asr at Arafat without a khutbah. The ruling: the prayer is valid (ajra).
The word 'ajra' indicates the prayer is accepted and valid.
2
Locate the reason
The author states that the khutbah is not fard (an obligation). This is the basis for the validity – since it is not obligatory, its omission does not harm the prayer.
In Hanafi usul, fard necessitates validity being affected if omitted; sunnah does not.
3
Distinguish from Jumu'ah
Contrast this with the Friday khutbah, which is a condition (shart) for Jumu'ah. The Arafat khutbah is only sunnah muakkadah, not a condition.
This distinction prevents mixing up the rulings for different prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ صَلَّى بِغَيْرِ حُطَبَةٍ أَجْراً وَلِأَنَّ هَذِهِ الْحُطَّبَةَ لَيْسَتْ بِفَرِيضَةٍ
So if he prays without a khutbah, it is valid, and because this khutbah is not an obligation (fard).
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This short passage presents a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: the khutbah delivered before the combined prayer on the Day of Arafah is not a fard (obligatory) component. If the imam omits it, the prayer is still valid. This distinguishes the 'Arafah khutbah from the Friday (Jumu'ah) khutbah, which is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer. The khutbah at Arafah is considered sunnah or mandub (recommended). The reasoning given is simply that it is not fard, implying that the primary obligation is the prayer itself and the standing at 'Arafah.

Key Terms
خُطْبَة (khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam before the combined prayer on the Day of Arafah.
فَرِيضَة (faridah): An obligation; a ruling whose omission invalidates the act or incurs sin if neglected without excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if the imam at Arafat prays the combined prayer without delivering a khutbah, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and the khutbah is not required.
C) The imam must make up the khutbah later.
D) The prayer is valid but the congregation must compensate with extra prayers.

Key Takeaway
The Arafat khutbah is not fard; the combined prayer is valid even without it.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Combining Prayers for an Individual at Arafat
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining Zuhr and 'Asr for an individual

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on combining prayers for an individual at Arafat and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Combining prayers at Arafat is a limited concession: only for the congregation behind the imam, not for individuals.

This passage from Al-Hidayah reveals a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the scope of the concession to combine Zuhr and 'Asr at Arafat. Understanding why Abu Hanifa restricts this to congregational prayer is crucial for correctly applying the school's rulings during Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core act and the dispute
The act is combining Zuhr and 'Asr at the time of Zuhr on the Day of Arafat. The dispute is whether an individual who prays Zuhr alone in his lodging (not in the main congregation) may also combine.
Focus on the 'individual' (munfarid) as the subject of the dispute.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his evidence
Abu Hanifa rules that such a person must pray 'Asr in its own time. His evidence: preserving the prayer time is fard by nusus; the concession is only for the congregation because the rationale is to relieve them from gathering again after dispersion.
Abu Hanifa also makes the imam a condition for both prayers.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the individual may combine. They reason that the need for prolonged standing (wuquf) applies to everyone, not just the congregation.
Zufar agrees with the condition of the imam but only for 'Asr.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa rejects their 'illa, insisting the true reason is the difficulty of gathering the congregation for 'Asr after dispersion. The individual faces no such difficulty, so the exception does not extend.
He also argues that combining is against qiyas, so it must be restricted to the explicit case.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if someone prays Zuhr alone, Abu Hanifa says he prays 'Asr separately; the Sahibayn say he can combine. The mufta bihi in the school is Abu Hanifa's view.
This affects a pilgrim's actual practice on Arafat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ صَلَّى الظُّهَرَ فِى رَحْلِهِ وَحْدَهُ صَلَّى الْعَصْرَ فِي وَقْتِهِ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا يَجْمَعُ بَيْنَهُمَا الْمُنْفَرِدُ لِأَنَّ جَوَازُ الْجَمِعِ لِلْحَاجَةِ إِلى إِمْتِدَادِ الْوُقُوفِ وَالْمُنْفَرِدُ مُحْتَاجُ إِلَيْهِ وَلا بِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ الْمُحَافَظَةَ عَلَى الْوَقْتِ فَرْضٌ بالتصوصِ فَلَا يَجُوزُ تَرَكُهُ الأَفِيْمَا وَرَدَ الشَّرْعُ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْجَمْعِ بِالْجَمَاعَةِ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ وَالتَّقْدِيمُ لِصِيَانَةِ الْجَمَاعَةِ لِأَنَّهُ يَعْسِرُ عَلَيْهِم الاجْتِمَاعُ لِلْعَصْرِ بَعْدَ مَا تَفَرَّقُوا فِى الْمَوْقِفِ لَا لِمَا ذَكَرَاهِ إِدْلَامَنَا فَاةَ ثُمَّ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ الإِمَامُ شَرطُ فِى الصَّلاتَيْنِ جَمِيعًا وَ قَالَ زُفْرُ فِى الْعَصْرِ حَاضَةَ لِأنَّهُ هُوَ المُغَيَّر عن وقته وعلى هذا الْخِلَافِ الإِحْرَامِ بِالْحَقِّ وَلِأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ التَّقْدِيمَ عَلَى خِلَافِ القَيَاسِ عُرِفَتْ شَرْعِيَّتُهُ فِيمَا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْعَصْرُ مُرَتَّبَةً عَلَى طَهْرٍ مُؤَدُّى بِالْجَمَاعَةِ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ فِي حَالَةِ الْإِحْرَامِ بِالْحَجِّ فَيَقْتَصِر عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ لَابُدَّ مِنَ الْإِحْرَامِ بِالْحَج قبلِ الزَّوَالِ فِي رِوَايَةٍ تَقْدِيمَا لِلإِحْرَامِ عَلَى وَقْتِ الْجَمْع وَفِي أَخْرَى يَكْتَفِى بِالتَّقْدِيمِ عَلَى الصَّلوةِ لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ هُوَ الصَّلوة
He said: And whoever prays Zuhr at his lodging alone, he prays 'Asr in its time according to Abu Hanifa. And (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The individual also combines between them because the permission to combine is due to the need for prolonging the standing, and the individual also needs that. And Abu Hanifa's evidence is that preserving the time is a fard by texts, so it is not permissible to leave it except in what the Shari'ah has permitted, which is combining in congregation with the imam. And the advancement (of 'Asr) is to protect the congregation because it is difficult for them to gather for 'Asr after they have dispersed in the place of standing, not for the reason they mentioned, since there is no contradiction. Then according to Abu Hanifa, the imam is a condition for both prayers. And Zufar said: (It is a condition) specifically for 'Asr because it is the one changed from its time. And upon this difference is the ihram for Hajj. And for Abu Hanifa, the advancement is against analogy (qiyas); its legality is known only when 'Asr is performed after Zuhr performed in congregation with the imam while in the state of ihram for Hajj, so it is limited to that. Then it is necessary that ihram for Hajj be before zawal (noon) in one narration, to give precedence to ihram over the time of combining, and in another narration, it is sufficient to give precedence to the prayer because the purpose is the prayer.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about the scope of the permission to combine Zuhr and 'Asr at Arafat. The issue is whether combining is restricted to those praying in congregation behind the imam or whether an individual who prays Zuhr alone in his lodging (i.e., not in the main congregation at the masjid) can also combine. Abu Hanifa holds that the individual must pray 'Asr in its own time (i.e., not combine). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the individual may also combine, reasoning that the rationale for combining is the need for prolonged standing at Arafat (which applies to everyone). Abu Hanifa counters that the rationale is to protect the congregation from the difficulty of gathering again for 'Asr after dispersion, not the need for standing per se. For an individual, there is no such difficulty. Furthermore, Abu Hanifa insists that the imam is a condition for both prayers in this combining; i.e., the combination is only valid when led by the imam. Imam Zufar agrees that the imam is a condition, but only for 'Asr because it is the prayer moved from its time. The passage also connects this to the timing of ihram for Hajj, explaining that ihram must be made before zawal (noon) in one narration to ensure it precedes the time of combining, while another narration suffices with ihram before the prayer itself, since the prayer is the objective. The overall ruling from Abu Hanifa is that the combination is an exception to the general rule (qiyas) and must be restricted to the specific scenario of congregation with the imam during Hajj.

Key Terms
جَمْع (jam'): Combining two prayers at the time of the earlier one (here Zuhr and 'Asr at Arafat).
مُنْفَرِد (munfarid): An individual who prays alone, not in congregation with the imam.
إِمَام (imam): The leader of the congregational prayer; for combining at Arafat, Abu Hanifa requires the imam of the Hajj congregation.
قِيَاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings; here, combining before time is against qiyas, so it is restricted to the explicit text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person prays Zuhr alone at his lodging on the Day of Arafat, when should he pray 'Asr?
A) He may combine 'Asr with Zuhr at the time of Zuhr.
B) He must pray 'Asr in its own time (i.e., not combine).
C) He must join the congregation for 'Asr only.
D) He cannot pray 'Asr at all.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa restricts the concession of combining at Arafat to those praying in congregation behind the imam; the individual must pray each prayer in its proper time.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Combining Prayers for the Individual on Arafah Day
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining prayers for the solitary pilgrim on Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on combining prayers for the solitary pilgrim on Arafah and evaluate the evidenciary basis for each view.

Core Idea
Combining prayers on Arafah requires congregation with the Imam; the solitary pilgrim may not combine in Abu Hanifa's view.

This lesson examines a famous intra-Hanafi dispute over the permissibility of combining Zuhr and Asr on the Day of Arafah for a pilgrim who prays Zuhr alone in his camp. The matn from Al-Hidayah presents the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and contrasts it with the views of his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school restricts a concession (rukhsah) to its specific occasion and how differing interpretations of the underlying rationale lead to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and Abu Hanifa's position
Identify the core legal question: may a pilgrim who prayed Zuhr alone combine Asr with it on Arafah? According to Abu Hanifa, he must pray Asr in its own time; combining is only allowed if both prayers are performed in congregation with the Imam (the caliph or his deputy).
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hidayah.
2
Identify the opposing views of the Sahibayn and Zufar
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the individual may combine, as the rationale (illah) for the concession is extending the standing at Arafah (wuquf), which applies equally to the solitary pilgrim. Zufar holds a middle view: the Imam is a condition only for Asr, since it is the prayer shifted from its time.
The Sahibayn reject the condition of congregation altogether for the permissibility of combining.
3
Examine the dalil of each side
Abu Hanifa's proof: Quranic verses (2:238, 4:103) making preservation of prayer times a fard; thus leaving the prescribed time is impermissible except where Shari'ah explicitly allows it—here only when praying in congregation with the Imam. The Sahibayn's proof: the illah for combining is the need to extend wuquf, which is equally present for the individual; therefore the concession is not tied to congregation.
The Hidayah attributes the Sahibayn's reasoning to 'imtidad al-wuquf' and critiques it.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn
The Hidayah argues that the true purpose of advancing Asr is to preserve the congregation (siyanat al-jama'ah), not to extend wuquf. There is no conflict between prayer and wuquf. The concession is a departure from analogy (khilaf al-qiyas) and must be restricted to its specific occasion: congregation with the Imam in the state of ihram for Hajj.
This response is based on the principle that any ruling contrary to qiyas is confined to its exact situation.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: a pilgrim who prays Zuhr alone at his camp on Arafah must, according to Abu Hanifa, pray Asr in its own time (delaying Asr). According to the Sahibayn, he may combine Asr with Zuhr. Zufar's view would allow combination if the Imam leads Asr alone. This difference also extends to the condition of ihram: Abu Hanifa requires ihram for both prayers; Zufar only for Asr; the Sahibayn require ihram but not the Imam.
The Hidayah does not explicitly resolve the ikhtilaf, but the mufta bihi in the later tradition follows Abu Hanifa.

قَالَ وَمَنْ صَلَّى الظُهْرَ فِى رَحْلِهِ وَحْدَهُ صَلَّى الْعَصْرَ فِي وَقْتِهِ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا يَجْمَعُ بَيْنَهُمَا الْمُنْفَرِدُ لِأَنَّ جَوَازُ الْجَمِعِ لِلْحَاجَةِ إِلى إِمْتِدَادِ الْوُقُوفِ وَالْمُنْفَرِدُ مُحْتَاجُ إِلَيْهِ وَلا بِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ الْمُحَافَظَةَ عَلَى الْوَقْتِ فَرْضٌ بِالتَّصُوصِ [؟] فَلَا يَجُوزُ تَرَكُهُ الأَفِيْمَا وَرَدَ الشَّرْعُ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْجَمْعِ بِالْجَمَاعَةِ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ وَالتَّقْدِيمُ لِصِيَانَةِ الْجَمَاعَةِ لِأَنَّهُ يَعْسِرُ عَلَيْهِم الاجْتِمَاعُ لِلْعَصْرِ بَعْدَ مَا تَفَرَّقُوا فِى الْمَوْقِفِ لَا لِمَا ذَكَرَاهِ إِذْ لَا مَنَافَاةَ [؟] ثُمَّ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ الإِمَامُ شَرطُ فِى الصَّلاتَيْنِ جَمِيعًا وَ قَالَ زُفْرُ فِى الْعَصْرِ خَاصَّةً [؟] لِأنَّهُ هُوَ المُغَيَّر عن وقته وعلى هذا الْخِلَافِ الإِحْرَامِ بِالْحَجِّ [؟] وَلِأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ التَّقْدِيمَ عَلَى خِلَافِ القَيَاسِ عُرِفَتْ شَرْعِيَّتُهُ فِيمَا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْعَصْرُ مُرَتَّبَّةً عَلَى طَهْرٍ مُؤَدَّى بِالْجَمَاعَةِ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ فِي حَالَةِ الْإِحْرَامِ بِالْحَجِّ فَيَقْتَصِر عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ لَابُدَّ مِنَ الْإِحْرَامِ بِالْحَج قبلِ الزَّوَالِ فِي رِوَايَةٍ تَقْدِيمَا لِلإِحْرَامِ عَلَى وَقْتِ الْجَمْع وَفِي أَخْرَى يَكْتَفِى بِالتَّقْدِيمِ عَلَى الصَّلوةِ لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ هُوَ الصَّلوة
ترجمہ اور جس نے ظہر کی نماز اپنی منزل میں تنہا پڑھی تو وہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک عصر کو اپنے وقت پر پڑھے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ تنہا پڑھنے والا بھی دونوں نمازوں کو جمع کرے۔ اس لئے کہ جمع کا جائز ہونا وقوف عرفہ کے دراز ہونے کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور منفرد بھی اس کا محتاج ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وقت پر محافظت کرنا نصوص قرآن سے فرض ہے لہذا اس کو ترک کرنا جائز نہیں ہے ۔ مگر اس صورت میں جس پر شریعت وارد ہوئی اور وہ امام کے ساتھ جماعت سے جمع کرنا ہے۔ اور عصر کو مقدم کرنا جماعت کی حفاظت کے لئے ہے۔ کیونکہ موقف میں متفرق ہونے کے بعد لوگوں پر عصر کے لئے جمع ہونا دشوار ہوگا۔ نہ اس وجہ سے جو صاحبین نے ذکر کیا ہے کیونکہ کچھ منافات نہیں ہے۔ پھر امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک دونوں نمازوں میں امام شرط ہے۔ اور امام زفر نے کہا کہ خاص کر عصر میں شرط ہے کیونکہ وہی اپنے وقت سے متغیر ہے۔ اور اسی اختلاف پر حج کا احرام ہے۔ اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عصر کو خلاف قیاس مقدم کرنا ایسی صورت میں مشروع ہونا معلوم ہوا ہے جبکہ عصر ایسی ظہر پر مرتب ہو جو حج کے احترام کی حالت میں امام کے ساتھ جماعت سے ادا کی گئی ہو یس اسی پر منحصر ہوگا۔ پھر ایک روایت میں حج کے احرام کا زوال سے پہلے ہونا ضروری ہے تا کہ احرام وقت جمع پر مقدم ہو جائے۔ اور دوسری روایت میں نماز پر مقدم کرنا کافی ہے کیونکہ مقصود تو نماز ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی حاجی نے ظہر کی نماز اپنے ٹھکانے پر تنہا پڑھ لی تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ شخص عصر کی نماز اس کے وقت میں ادا کرے یعنی ظہر و عصر کو ظہر کے وقت میں جمع نہ کرے۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ تنہا پڑھنے والا بھی دونوں نمازوں کو جمع کرے۔ یعنی منفرد اور باجماعت پڑھنے والا جمع بین الصلاتین کے حکم میں دونوں برابر ہیں۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ میدان عرفات میں حاجی کے لئے ظہر و عصر کو جمع کرنے کی اجازت اس لئے دی گئی ہے تا کہ وقوف عرفہ زیادہ سے زیادہ کر سکے۔ یعنی وقوف عرفہ دراز کرنے کی وجہ سے جمع بین الصلاتین کی اجازت دی گئی ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ جس پر وقوف فرض نہیں اس کے لئے جمع بین الصلاتین کی بھی اجازت نہیں ہے ۔ اور اس ضرورت میں منفرد اور باجماعت نماز ادا کرنے والا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اس لئے جمع بین الصلاتین کا حکم دونوں کے لئے یکساں ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وقت کے اندر نماز کی محافظت فرض ہے جیسا کہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے حَافِظُوا عَلَى الصَّلَوَاتِ وَالصَّلوةِ الوسطى (البقرة:۲۳۸) اور اِنَّ الصَّلوةَ كَانَتْ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ كِتبًا مَّوْقُوتًا (النساء:۱۰۳) اور جو چیز نصوص قرآنی سے ثابت ہو اس کا ترک کرنا جائز نہیں ہے الا یہ کہ اس کے خلاف شریعت وارد ہوئی ہو۔ اور شریعت کا ورود اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ امام کے ساتھ جماعت سے نماز ادا کی جائے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ اگر یوم عرفہ میں حاجی ظہر و عصر کو باجماعت ادا کرتا ہے تب تو عصر کو اس کے وقت پر مقدم کر کے جمع بین الصلاتین کی اجازت ہے ورنہ نہیں۔
وَالتَّقْدِيمُ لِصِيَّانَة ... الخ سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ عصر کی نماز کو اس کے وقت پر مقدم کرنا امتداد وقوف کی وجہ سے نہیں جیسا کہ صاحبین نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ نماز اور وقوف کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں دونوں اکٹھا ہو سکتے ہیں بلکہ عصر کو مقدم کرنا جماعت کی حفاظت کے پیش نظر ہے۔ کیونکہ ظہر پڑھ کو لوگ اگر میدان عرفات میں منتشر ہو گئے تو عصر کے لئے ان کو جمع کرنا بہت دشوار ہو گا۔ پس اس دشواری کی وجہ سے اور فضیلت جماعت کو حاصل کرنے کی وجہ سے عصر کو اس کے وقت پر مقدم کر کے ظہر و عصر کو جمع کرنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ان دونوں نمازوں میں امام اعظم کے نزدیک امام المسلمین یا اس کے نائب کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ امام زفر نے کہا کہ خاص طور پر عصر میں شرط ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ امام کسی میں شرط نہیں ہے۔ یہی اختلاف حج کے احرام میں ہے۔ یعنی امام صاحب کے نزدیک دونوں نمازیں جمع کرنے کے لئے حج کا احرام شرط ہے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک فقط عصر کی نماز میں احرام حج شرط ہے۔ ثمرہ اختلاف یہ ہے کہ ایک حلال ( غیر محرم) نے امام کے ساتھ ظہر کی نماز پڑھی پھر اس نے حج کا احرام باندھ لیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک عصر کو ظہر کے وقت میں ادا کرنا جائز نہیں اور امام زفر کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک جمع بین الصلاتین کا جواز دونوں نمازوں میں احرام حج پر معلق ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک احرام، جماعت اور امام المسلمین پر معلق ہے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک یہ سب شرطیں فقط عصر کی نماز میں ہیں۔
صاحبین کی دلیل تو ظاہر ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک جمع بین الصلاتین کے لئے جماعت شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ منفرد بھی ان دونوں نمازوں کو جمع کرے گا۔ پس جب جماعت ہی شرط نہیں تو امام یا اس کے نائب کی شرط کیونکر ہوگی۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عصر کی نماز اپنے وقت سے بدل گئی ہے اور تغیر ہی کی وجہ سے امام کی شرط ہے۔ اس لئے خاص کر عصر کی نماز میں امام کا ہونا شرط ہے ظہر کی نماز میں شرط نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عصر کی نماز کو اس کے وقت پر مقدم کرنا خلاف قیاس اس صورت میں مشروع ہوا ہے، جبکہ عصر کی نماز کا ترتب ایسی ظہر پر ہو جس کو حج کے احترام کی حالت میں امام کے ساتھ جماعت سے ادا کیا گیا ہو۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو چیز خلاف قیاس مشروع ہو وہ اپنے مورد پر منحصر رہتی ہے اور مورد شرع یہ ہے کہ میدان عرفات میں نویں ذی الحجہ کو امام کے ساتھ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز ادا کی گئی ہے اور حج کے احرام کی حالت میں ادا کی گئی ہے۔ پس تا قیامت ان شرطوں کو لازم رکھنا ضروری ہوگا۔ حتی کہ اگر کوئی ایک شرط نہ پائی گئی تو جمع بین
He said: Whoever prays Zuhr in his camp alone, prays Asr in its time according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The one praying alone combines them because the permissibility of combining is due to the need for extending the stay (wuquf), and the individual also needs that. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that preserving the time is a fard by texts, so it is not permissible to leave it except in what the Shari'ah has allowed, which is combining in congregation with the Imam. And he said: The reason is the preservation of the congregation because it is difficult for them to gather for Asr after they have dispersed at the standing place, not for what they (the two) mentioned, as there is no conflict. Then according to Abu Hanifa, the Imam is a condition in both prayers. Zufar said: specifically in Asr, because it is the one changed from its time. And on this difference is the ihram for Hajj. And for Abu Hanifa that advancing (Asr) contrary to analogy is known from Shari'ah when Asr is ordered after a prayer performed in congregation with the Imam in a state of ihram for Hajj, so it is limited to that. Then it is necessary to have ihram before zawal in one narration to advance the ihram over the time of combining, and in another it is sufficient to advance it over the prayer because the objective is the prayer. (The rest is Urdu commentary elaborating the dispute.)
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) on the permissibility of combining Zuhr and Asr prayers (jama' bayn al-salatayn) on the Day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) for a pilgrim who prayed Zuhr alone in his camp (rahli). The matn from Al-Hidayah presents the differing views. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, such a person must pray Asr in its own time and cannot combine; combining is only permitted if the prayers are offered in congregation (jama'ah) with the Imam (the caliph or his deputy). The two disciples (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the individual may also combine, because the reason for the concession is the need to prolong the standing at Arafah (wuquf), which applies equally to the individual and the congregation. Imam Zufar holds a middle view: the Imam is a condition only for Asr, since it is the prayer shifted from its time. The text then explains the proofs: Abu Hanifa cites the Quranic command to guard the prayers (Surah al-Baqarah 2:238) and that prayer is prescribed at fixed times (Surah al-Nisa 4:103), implying that leaving the prescribed time is impermissible except where Shari'ah explicitly allows it, which is only when praying in congregation with the Imam. The rationale given in the Hidayah is that the advanced performance of Asr is not to extend wuquf (as the Sahibayn claim) but to protect the congregation (jam'ah) from the difficulty of gathering after dispersal. The commentary further notes that this difference extends to the condition of ihram for Hajj: Abu Hanifa requires ihram for combining both prayers, Zufar only for Asr, and the Sahibayn require ihram for both but not the Imam. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that if a person who is not in ihram (halal) prays Zuhr with the Imam and then assumes ihram, Abu Hanifa would not allow him to combine Asr, while Zufar would.

Key Terms
جمع بين الصلاتين (jama' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two prayers (Zuhr and Asr) into one time on the Day of Arafah.
منفرد (mufrad): A person praying alone, not in congregation.
وقوف عرفة (wuquf Arafah): The standing on the plain of Arafah on the 9th Dhul Hijjah, a rukn of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is required for the permissibility of combining Zuhr and Asr on the Day of Arafah?
A) The prayer must be offered in congregation with the Imam while in the state of ihram.
B) The pilgrim must be praying alone.
C) The time of Zuhr must be extended.
D) The prayers must be offered at the camp (rahl).

Key Takeaway
Combining prayers on Arafah is a concession (rukhsah) limited to its specific occasion: congregation with the Imam in the state of ihram.

Conditions for Joining Zuhr and Asr at Arafah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on jam' at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam Zufar on the conditions for joining Zuhr and Asr at Arafah, and apply the principle that a ruling contrary to qiyas is confined to its specific case.

Core Idea
A Shari'ah concession contrary to qiyas remains confined to its original conditions; joining requires congregation and ihram.

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about the conditions for joining Zuhr and Asr on the Day of Arafah. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents three distinct positions within the Hanafi school regarding congregation, imam, and ihram. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply the usul principle that exceptions are not extended beyond their original context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi positions and their conditions
List the conditions required by each imam: Abu Hanifa requires congregation behind the Imam of the Muslims (or his deputy) and ihram for both prayers; the Sahibayn require ihram for both but not congregation; Zufar requires these conditions only for Asr.
Note that the dispute is over whether congregation, imam, and ihram are conditions for both prayers or just Asr.
2
Determine the evidence (dalil) for each position
Imam Abu Hanifa cites Quranic verses (2:238, 4:103) on preserving prayer times and argues that the exception is only for the specific case of the Prophet's practice. The Sahibayn argue that the purpose is to prolong wuquf, which applies equally to individuals and congregations. Zufar focuses on Asr being shifted from its time.
Identify which proofs are textual (Quran/Hadith) and which are based on legal reasoning (qiyas, istihsan).
3
Analyse the point of dispute and the principle of 'khilaf al-qiyas'
Imam Abu Hanifa's position rests on the principle that a ruling contrary to analogy (khilaf al-qiyas) is restricted to its original case. Advancing Asr is not due to wuquf prolongation but to preserve congregation, so congregation is necessary.
Consider why the Sahibayn disagree: they see the ruling as based on the benefit of prolonging wuquf, which is general.
4
Work through the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The example: a non-muhrim prays Zuhr with the imam, then enters ihram. According to Abu Hanifa, he cannot join Asr with Zuhr because he lacked ihram at Zuhr. According to Zufar, he can join because the conditions apply only to Asr.
The thamarah shows the real-world impact of the different rulings.
5
Evaluate which position is mufta bihi and why
The relied-upon position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as it is the most cautious and aligns with the principle of restricting exceptions. The Hidayah presents all views but implies the dominant position.
Understanding the tarjih helps know the operative ruling for fatwa.

جمع کرے۔ یعنی منفرد اور باجماعت پڑھنے والا جمع بین الصلاتین کے حکم میں دونوں برابر ہیں۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ میدان عرفات میں حاجی کے لئے ظہر و عصر کو جمع کرنے کی اجازت اس لئے دی گئی ہے تا کہ وقوف عرفہ زیادہ سے زیادہ کر سکے۔ یعنی وقوف عرفہ دراز کرنے کی وجہ سے جمع بین الصلاتین کی اجازت دی گئی ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ جس پر وقوف فرض نہیں اس کے لئے جمع بین الصلاتین کی بھی اجازت نہیں ہے ۔ اور اس ضرورت میں منفرد اور باجماعت نماز ادا کرنے والا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اس لئے جمع بین الصلاتین کا حکم دونوں کے لئے یکساں ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وقت کے اندر نماز کی محافظت فرض ہے جیسا کہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے حَافِظُوا عَلَى الصَّلَوَاتِ وَالصَّلوةِ الوسطى (البقرة:۲۳۸) اور اِنَّ الصَّلوةَ كَانَتْ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ كِتبًا مَّوْقُوتًا (الماء (۱۰۳)- اور جو چیز نصوص قرآنی سے ثابت ہو اس کا ترک کرنا جائز نہیں ہے الا یہ کہ اس کے خلاف شریعت وارد ہوئی ہو۔ اور شریعت کا ورود اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ امام کے ساتھ جماعت سے نماز ادا کی جائے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ اگر یوم عرفہ میں حاجی ظہر و عصر کو باجماعت ادا کرتا ہے تب تو عصر کو اس کے وقت پر مقدم کر کے جمع بین الصلاتین کی اجازت ہے ورنہ نہیں۔
وَالتَّقْدِيمُ لِصِيَّانَة ... الخ سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ عصر کی نماز کو اس کے وقت پر مقدم کرنا امتداد وقوف کی وجہ سے نہیں جیسا کہ صاحبین نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ نماز اور وقوف کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں دونوں اکٹھا ہو سکتے ہیں بلکہ عصر کو مقدم کرنا جماعت کی حفاظت کے پیش نظر ہے۔ کیونکہ ظہر پڑھ کو لوگ اگر میدان عرفات میں منتشر ہو گئے تو عصر کے لئے ان کو جمع کرنا بہت دشوار ہو گا۔ پس اس دشواری کی وجہ سے اور فضیلت جماعت کو حاصل کرنے کی وجہ سے عصر کو اس کے وقت پر مقدم کر کے ظہر و عصر کو جمع کرنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ان دونوں نمازوں میں امام اعظم کے نزدیک امام المسلمین یا اس کے نائب کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ امام زفر نے کہا کہ خاص طور پر عصر میں شرط ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ امام کسی میں شرط نہیں ہے۔ یہی اختلاف حج کے احرام میں ہے۔ یعنی امام صاحب کے نزدیک دونوں نمازیں جمع کرنے کے لئے حج کا احرام شرط ہے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک فقط عصر کی نماز میں احرام حج شرط ہے۔ ثمرہ اختلاف یہ ہے کہ ایک حلال ( غیر محرم) نے امام کے ساتھ ظہر کی نماز پڑھی پھر اس نے حج کا احرام باندھ لیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک عصر کو ظہر کے وقت میں ادا کرنا جائز نہیں اور امام زفر کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک جمع بین الصلاتین کا جواز دونوں نمازوں میں احرام حج پر معلق ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک احترام، جماعت اور امام المسلمین پر معلق ہے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک یہ سب شرطیں فقط عصر کی نماز میں ہیں۔
صاحبین کی دلیل تو ظاہر ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک جمع بین الصلاتین کے لئے جماعت شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ منفرد بھی ان دونوں نمازوں کو جمع کرے گا۔ پس جب جماعت ہی شرط نہیں تو امام یا اس کے نائب کی شرط کیونکر ہوگی۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عصر کی نماز اپنے وقت سے بدل گئی ہے اور تغیر ہی کی وجہ سے امام کی شرط ہے۔ اس لئے خاص کر عصر کی نماز میں امام کا ہونا شرط ہے ظہر کی نماز میں شرط نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عصر کی نماز کو اس کے وقت پر مقدم کرنا خلاف قیاس اس صورت میں مشروع ہوا ہے، جبکہ عصر کی نماز کا ترتب ایسی ظہر پر ہو جس کو حج کے احترام کی حالت میں امام کے ساتھ جماعت سے ادا کیا گیا ہو۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو چیز خلاف قیاس مشروع ہو وہ اپنے مورد پر منحصر رہتی ہے اور مور د شرع یہ ہے کہ میدان عرفات میں نویں ذی الحجہ کو امام کے ساتھ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز ادا کی گئی ہے اور حج کے احرام کی حالت میں ادا کی گئی ہے۔ پس تا قیامت ان شرطوں کو کو ظ رکھنا ضروری ہوگا۔ حتی کہ اگر کوئی ایک شرط نہ پائی گئی تو جمع بین الصلوتین کا جواز ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
He combines. That is, the one praying alone and with congregation are equal in the ruling of joining prayers. The evidence of the Sahibayn is that the permission for the pilgrim to combine Zuhr and Asr in the plain of Arafat was given so that he can prolong the wuquf at Arafah. That is, permission for joining was given due to lengthening the wuquf at Arafah, and for this reason, the one upon whom wuquf is not obligatory does not have permission to join. In this need, the one praying alone and with congregation are equal. Therefore, the ruling of joining will be the same for both. The evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa is that preserving prayer within its time is obligatory, as Allah said: "Guard strictly the prayers, especially the middle prayer" (2:238) and "Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers at prescribed times" (4:103). And whatever is established by Quranic texts, it is not permissible to abandon it unless a [contrary] ruling from the Shari'ah occurs. And the occurrence from Shari'ah is only when prayer is performed with an imam in congregation. Thus, it is established that if on the Day of Arafah the pilgrim performs Zuhr and Asr with congregation, then it is permitted to advance Asr and join; otherwise, not. ... from "And the advancing is to preserve..." is the response to the evidence of the Sahibayn. The gist of the response is that advancing the Asr prayer from its time is not due to the prolongation of wuquf as the Sahibayn mentioned, because there is no contradiction between prayer and wuquf; both can be done together. Rather, advancing Asr is for the preservation of congregation, because after praying Zuhr, if people disperse in the plain of Arafat, it would be very difficult to gather them for Asr. Due to this difficulty and to attain the virtue of congregation, it was prescribed to advance Asr and combine Zuhr and Asr. The author of Hidayah says that according to Imam al-A'zam, in both prayers, the presence of the Imam of the Muslims or his deputy is a condition. Imam Zufar said that it is a condition specifically in Asr. And the Sahibayn said that the imam is not a condition in either. The same difference exists regarding the ihram of Hajj. That is, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, for combining both prayers, ihram of Hajj is a condition, and according to Imam Zufar, ihram of Hajj is a condition only in the Asr prayer. The practical consequence is that a halal (non-muhrim) person prayed Zuhr with the imam, then he entered ihram for Hajj. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not permissible for him to perform Asr in the time of Zuhr, while according to Imam Zufar, it is permissible. The conclusion is that according to the Sahibayn, permissibility of joining in both prayers depends on ihram of Hajj; according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it depends on ihram, congregation, and the Imam of the Muslims; and according to Imam Zufar, all these conditions are only in the Asr prayer. The evidence of the Sahibayn is apparent: according to them, congregation is not a condition for joining, even a lone person will combine both prayers. So when congregation is not a condition, how can the condition of an imam or his deputy be? The evidence of Imam Zufar is that the Asr prayer has been changed from its time, and due to this change, the condition of an imam is required. Therefore, the presence of an imam is specifically a condition for Asr, not for Zuhr. The evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa is that advancing the Asr prayer from its time is contrary to qiyas and was legislated only in the case where the Asr prayer follows a Zuhr prayer that was performed with the imam in congregation while in the state of ihram. And the principle is that whatever is legislated contrary to qiyas remains confined to its specific case. And the occurrence of Shari'ah is that on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah in the plain of Arafat, prayer was performed with the imam in congregation and while in the state of ihram. Thus, until the Day of Judgment, preserving these conditions is necessary. Even if one condition is missing, the permissibility of joining falls away.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions for joining Zuhr and Asr prayers at Arafah on the Day of Arafah. The dispute involves Imam Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and Imam Zufar. The focus is on three conditions: congregation (jama'ah), presence of the imam or his deputy, and the state of ihram for Hajj.

First, the passage explains the Sahibayn's position. They argue that the permission to join is given to allow pilgrims to prolong wuquf. Since this benefit applies equally to those praying alone and in congregation, congregation is not a condition for joining. Therefore, the imam's presence is also not required.

Imam Abu Hanifa holds that prayer must be performed within its prescribed time as per the Quran. The only exception is when a specific Shari'ah concession exists. That concession is established for a person praying in congregation behind an imam at Arafah. Thus, congregation and the imam are necessary conditions. He also requires ihram for Hajj for both prayers.

Imam Zufar takes an intermediate position: only the Asr prayer is moved from its time, so the conditions of imam, congregation, and ihram apply only to Asr, not Zuhr.

The passage then details the evidence of each. The Sahibayn cite the purpose of prolonging wuquf and the absence of a distinction between congregational and individual prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa cites Quranic verses on preserving prayers and the principle that exceptions are confined to their specific case. Imam Zufar focuses on the change specific to Asr.

The practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf) is illustrated: a non-muhrim prays Zuhr with the imam, then enters ihram. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he cannot join Asr with Zuhr because he lacked ihram at the time of Zuhr. According to Imam Zufar, he can, since ihram is only required for Asr.

Finally, the passage reinforces Imam Abu Hanifa's reliance on the principle that a ruling contrary to qiyas (analogy) is restricted to its original context. Since the joining was prescribed for the specific situation of the Prophet with congregation and ihram, these conditions must be present for the ruling to apply.

Key Terms
جمع بین الصلاتین (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Performing two prayers (Zuhr and Asr, or Maghrib and Isha) within the time of the earlier one (jam' taqdim) or later one (jam' ta'khir) at specific places and times.
موقف (mawqif): The place where pilgrims stand during wuquf at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.
وقوف (wuquf): The act of standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; the essential pillar of Hajj.
امام المسلمین (imam al-muslimin): The caliph or his deputy who leads the congregational prayers at Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, what conditions are necessary for joining Zuhr and Asr at Arafah?
A) Congregation behind the imam and ihram for Hajj for both prayers
B) Only ihram for Hajj for both prayers
C) Only congregation for Asr prayer
D) No conditions; joining is always permissible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position requires congregation behind the Imam of the Muslims and the state of ihram for both prayers when joining Zuhr and Asr at Arafah.

Requirement of Ihram Before Zawal for Joining Prayers
States the condition that ihram must precede zawal for joining prayers at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for joining prayers at Arafah and identify the two narrations regarding the timing of ihram.

Core Idea
For valid joining at Arafah, ihram must precede zawal — the condition must be in place before the conditioned begins.

The permissibility of joining Zuhr and Asr at Arafah is a special concession for pilgrims. However, this concession is conditional: the pilgrim must have entered the state of ihram before the sun passes its zenith (zawal). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this condition and introduces an alternative narration within the Hanafi school that offers a slightly different view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage states that joining prayers at Arafah is permissible only if the pilgrim has entered ihram before zawal. Recognize that this is a condition (shart) for validity.
2
Understand the logical principle
The principle is 'a condition precedes the conditioned' (الشرط مقدم على المشروط). Since the permissibility of joining begins at zawal, the condition (ihram) must be in place before that moment.
This is a fundamental usul al-fiqh principle.
3
Determine the practical implication
Because the permissibility of joining is effective from zawal, ihram must be performed before zawal. If ihram occurs after zawal, the condition is not met and joining is not permissible.
This is the primary view (zahir al-riwayah).
4
Recognize the alternative narration
An alternative narration (riwayah) holds that it is sufficient for ihram to precede the Zuhr prayer itself, not necessarily zawal. The reasoning is that the purpose is the prayer, not the time.
This provides flexibility, but the primary view is considered stronger.

Source Text

صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ عرفہ کے دن جمع بین الصلواتین کے جواز کے لئے حج کے احرام کا زوال سے پہلے ہونا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ احرام جمع بین الصلاتین کے جواز کی شرط ہے۔ اور شرط شی شی ، پر مقدم ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے احرام، جواز جمع پر مقدم ہوگا اور جواز جمع بین الصلوتین سورج ڈھلتے ہی متحقق ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ احترام زوال سے پہلے باندھا جائے تا کہ احرام کو جو از جمع پر تقدم حاصل ہو۔ اور ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ احرام کو زوال پر مقدم کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ نماز ظہر پر مقدم کرنا بھی کافی ہے کیونکہ مقصود تو نماز ہی ہے نہ کہ وقت اس لئے نماز پر مقدم ہونا کافی ہے، وقت زوال پر مقدم کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
The author of Hidayah has said that for the permissibility of joining the two prayers on the Day of Arafah, it is necessary for the ihram of Hajj to be before zawal. Because ihram is a condition for the permissibility of joining. And a condition precedes the conditioned thing. Therefore, ihram must precede the permissibility of joining. And the permissibility of joining occurs as soon as the sun declines, so it is necessary that ihram be performed before zawal so that ihram precedes the permissibility of joining. And there is a narration that it is not necessary for ihram to precede zawal. Rather, it is sufficient that it precede the Zuhr prayer, because the intended thing is the prayer, not the time. Therefore, preceding the prayer is sufficient; preceding the time of zawal is not necessary.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage explains a condition for joining prayers at Arafah: the pilgrim must have entered the state of ihram before zawal (midday). The reasoning is that ihram is a condition (shart) for the permissibility of joining, and conditions logically precede the conditioned. Since the permissibility of joining becomes effective at zawal (when Zuhr time begins), the condition (ihram) must be in place before that moment.

Then the passage presents an alternative narration (riwayah) that does not require ihram to precede zawal specifically; it is enough that ihram is done before the Zuhr prayer itself. The rationale is that the purpose is the prayer, not the mere time. So if one enters ihram after zawal but before praying Zuhr, it is acceptable according to this narration.

The ruling is part of the broader discussion on the conditions for jam' taqdim (advancing Asr to Zuhr time) at Arafah. The primary view (that of Imam Abu Hanifa) requires ihram before zawal, but the alternative view provides some flexibility.

Key Terms
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes the meridian, indicating the start of Zuhr time.
احرام (ihram): The sacred state of a pilgrim performing Hajj or Umrah, entered by wearing specific garments and making niyyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary ruling regarding the timing of ihram for joining prayers at Arafah?
A) Ihram must be before zawal
B) Ihram must be after zawal
C) Ihram must be before Maghrib
D) Ihram is not required for joining

Key Takeaway
The primary Hanafi position requires ihram before zawal for joining prayers at Arafah because the condition must precede the conditioned.

Location of Wuquf: Near the Mountain, Excluding Batn 'Arnah
Specifies the recommended location for wuquf and excludes Batn 'Arnah based on Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended location for wuquf at Arafat and identify the only area that is excluded, citing the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is a mawqif except Batn 'Arnah — standing there is prohibited by sunnah.

After completing the combined prayers at Arafat, the pilgrim proceeds to the mawqif. This lesson specifies where exactly one should stand — preferably near Jabal al-Rahmah — and clarifies the only area that must be avoided, based on a direct prophetic command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended location
Find in the passage that the imam and pilgrims head towards the mawqif immediately after prayer, and stand near the mountain called Jabal al-Rahmah.
This is the spot of the Prophet's wuquf, so it is a sunnah muakkadah.
2
Understand the exception
Note that the hadith excludes Batn 'Arnah from valid wuquf locations. All other parts of Arafat are acceptable.
The imperative 'irtifa'u' (avoid) indicates prohibition.
3
Learn the dalil
Memorize the hadith: 'All of Arafat is a mawqif, and avoid the valley of 'Arnah.' Recognize its zanni thubut but qati dalalah.
This is a key proof text for the Hanafi position.

قَالَ ثُمَّ يَتَوَجَّهُ إِلَى المَوقِفِ فَيَقِفُ بِقُرُبِ الْجَبَلِ وَالْقَوْمُ مَعَهُ عَقِيْبَ إِنصِرَافِهم مِنَ الصَّلوة لأنَّ النَّبِى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ رَاحَ إِلَى الْمَوْقَفِ عَقِيبَ الصَّلوةِ وَالْجَبَلُ يُسَمَّى جَبَلُ الرَّحْمَةِ والموقف موقف الأعظم
ترجمہ کہا کہ پھر موقف کی طرف متوجہ ہو پس پہاڑ کے نزدیک کھڑا ہو اور لوگ اسکے ساتھ ، نماز سے پھرتے ہی کیونکہ رسول اکرم ہے نماز کے بعد موقف کی طرف تشریف لے گئے اور پہاڑ کا نام جبل رحمت سے اور موقف کا نام موقف اعظم ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ، عرفات میں جمع بین الصلاتین سے فراغت کے بعد امام اور لوگ سب موقف میں چلے جائیں اور پہاڑ کے قریب جا کر کھڑے ہوں اس پہاڑ کا نام جبل رحمت اور موقف کا نام موقف اعظم ہے۔ حضور نے بھی اسی پہاڑ کے قریب وقوف فرمایا ہے۔ میدان سارے کا سارا وقوف کی جگہ ہے
قَالَ وَعَرَفَاتُ كُلُّهَا مَوْقَفٌ الأَبَطْنَ عُرنَة لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَرَفَاتٌ كُلُّهَا مَوَقَفٌ وَارْتَفَعُوا عَنْ بَطَنٍ عُرْنَةٍ والْمُرْدَلَفَةٌ كُلُّهَا مَوْقَفْ وَارْتَفَعُوا عَنْ وَادِى مُحَشَرٍ
ترجمہ کہا اور عرفات پورا موقف ہے سواء بطن عرنہ کے۔ کیونکہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ عرفات پورا موقف ہے اور وطن عرنہ سے اونچے رہو اور مزدلفہ پورا موقف ہے اور اٹھے رہووادی محسر سے۔
تشریح فرمایا کہ بطن عرنہ کے علاوہ پورا عرفات موقف ہے یعنی بطن عرنہ میں کھڑا نہ ہو باقی سب کھڑے ہونے کی جگہ ے۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بطن عرنہ میں شیطان کو دیکھا تھا اس لئے اس مقام میں کھڑا ہونے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اسی طرح وادی محسر کے علاوہ مزدلفہ پورے کا پورا موقف ہے۔
He said: Then he heads towards the mawqif and stands near the mountain, and the people with him, immediately after finishing the prayer, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) went to the mawqif immediately after prayer. The mountain is called Jabal al-Rahmah and the mawqif is called al-Mawqif al-A'zam.
Translation: He said: Then he heads towards the mawqif and stands near the mountain, and the people with him, immediately after finishing the prayer, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) went to the mawqif after prayer. The mountain is called Jabal al-Rahmah and the mawqif is called al-Mawqif al-A'zam.
Explanation: After finishing the joining of prayers at Arafah, the imam and all people should proceed to the mawqif and stand near the mountain. This mountain is called Jabal al-Rahmah and the mawqif is called al-Mawqif al-A'zam. The Prophet also performed wuquf near this mountain. The entire plain is a place for wuquf.
He said: And all of Arafat is a mawqif except Batn 'Arnah, because of his (peace be upon him) saying: "All of Arafat is a mawqif, and avoid the valley of 'Arnah." And all of Muzdalifah is a mawqif, and avoid the valley of Muhassir.
Translation: He said: And all of Arafat is a mawqif except Batn 'Arnah, because the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: "All of Arafat is a mawqif, and avoid the valley of 'Arnah." And all of Muzdalifah is a mawqif, and avoid the valley of Muhassir.
Explanation: He said that except for Batn 'Arnah, all of Arafat is a mawqif, meaning do not stand in Batn 'Arnah; the rest is a place for standing. Some scholars said that the Prophet (peace be upon him) saw Satan in Batn 'Arnah, so he forbade standing there. Similarly, except for the valley of Muhassir, all of Muzdalifah is a mawqif.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage provides practical guidance on the location of wuquf at Arafat. After completing the midday prayers (Zuhr and Asr combined), the imam and pilgrims proceed to the mawqif, specifically near a mountain called Jabal al-Rahmah (Mountain of Mercy). This is the very spot where the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed his wuquf. The entire plain of Arafat is permissible for wuquf, but there is one exception: the valley called Batn 'Arnah. Standing in this valley is not allowed. The evidence is a hadith: "All of Arafat is a mawqif, and avoid the valley of 'Arnah." The commentary adds that the Prophet saw Satan there, which is why it is prohibited. Similarly, for Muzdalifah, the entire area is a mawqif except the valley of Muhassir.

The term "mawqif" refers to the place of standing (wuquf). The specific spot near Jabal al-Rahmah is called al-Mawqif al-A'zam (the Greatest Standing Place). The lesson emphasizes following the sunnah by standing near this mountain, but also acknowledges that any part of Arafat (except Batn 'Arnah) suffices for wuquf.

Key Terms
موقف (mawqif): The place designated for wuquf (standing) during Hajj.
جبل الرحمة (Jabal al-Rahmah): A mountain in Arafat near which the Prophet stood; highly recommended for standing.
بطن عرنة (Batn 'Arnah): A valley in Arafat where standing is prohibited.
وادی محسر (Wadi Muhassir): A valley in Muzdalifah where standing is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Jabal al-Rahmah
B) Batn 'Arnah
C) Mawqif al-A'zam
D) The entire plain of Arafat

Key Takeaway
All of Arafat is a mawqif except Batn 'Arnah; standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is sunnah.

The Imam's Recommended Posture at Arafah
Recommendation with dalil from Prophet's practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended action for the imam during wuquf at Arafah and identify the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Standing on a mount facing qibla at Arafah is sunnah, not wajib.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the conduct of the imam during the most important rite of Hajj: the standing at Arafah. It clarifies that while standing on foot is permissible, the preferred practice, following the Prophet, is to be on a mount and face the qibla. The text emphasizes emulation of the Prophet as the basis for this recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon and its legal classification. The passage recommends that the imam stand on a riding animal (rāḥilah) and face the qibla.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the evidence cited. The author points to the Prophet's action (standing on his camel and facing qibla) as the basis for the recommendation.
The exact hadith is not quoted; the passage cuts off.
3
Note the Permissibility of Alternatives
Observe that standing on foot is explicitly allowed (jāza), but the first option is better (afḍal). This clarifies the hierarchy of preference.
The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
4
Understand the Preference
Recognize why the first option is afḍal: it follows the Prophet's practice more directly. The act of facing qibla is also recommended based on his example.
5
Acknowledge the Incomplete Text
The passage ends abruptly with 'wa qāla al-nabiyy…' indicating a missing hadith. This does not affect the ruling but shows the original source likely continued.

قَالَ وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ يَقِفَ بِعَرَفَةَ عَلَى رَاحِلَةٍ لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَقَفَ عَلى نَاقَتِهِ وَإِنَّ وَقَفَ عَلَى قَدَمَيْهِ جَازَ وَالْأَوَّلُ أَفْضَلَ لِمَا بَيْنَا وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَقِفَ مُسْتَقِيلَ الْقِبْلَةِ لِأَنَّ النَّبِى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَ قَفَ كَذلِكَ وَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ
He said: And it is fitting for the imam to stand at Arafah on a riding animal, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood on his camel. And if he stands on his feet, it is permissible, but the first is better as we have explained. And it is fitting that he stand facing the qibla, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood like that, and the Prophet said...
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage gives a recommended practice for the imam during wuquf at Arafah. It is mustahabb (preferred) for the imam to stand on a riding animal (like a camel) rather than on his feet, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did so. However, standing on foot is permissible, but the first is better. Additionally, it is recommended to face the qibla while performing wuquf, again following the Prophet's practice. The text cuts off after mentioning that the Prophet said something, likely a hadith about facing qibla.

The ruling is specifically for the imam, as he leads the pilgrims. The common pilgrim may also follow these recommendations, but the text focuses on the imam's conduct. The action is clearly a sunnah (recommended) based on the Prophet's example.

Key Terms
راحلة (rahilah): A riding animal, typically a camel, used for travel.
مستقبل القبلة (mustaqbil al-qiblah): Facing the direction of prayer (the Ka'bah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The imam's standing on a mount facing qibla at Arafah is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation, based on the Prophet's practice.

Proceeding to the Standing Place at Arafah
Ruling with proof: the imam's post-prayer movement to the standing place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (hukm) for the imam's movement to the standing place at Arafah and explain the proof from the Prophet's action.

Core Idea
The imam's immediate move to Jabal al-Rahmah is a sunnah, not a wajib.

This lesson examines a specific sunnah action of Hajj: the imam leading the congregation to the standing place (al-mawqif) right after the combined prayer at Arafah. The text specifies that they should stand near Jabal al-Rahmah, following the Prophet's example. Understanding the distinction between sunnah and wajib here is crucial for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
What is the imam doing immediately after the prayer? The text says he proceeds to the standing place and stands near the mountain.
The act is physically moving to a specific location.
2
Determine the ruling classification
Is this act fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.? The Hanafi position classifies it as sunnah muakkadah based on the Prophet's action.
Sunnah muakkadah means a strongly recommended but non-obligatory act.
3
Locate the proof
The author cites the Prophet's action: 'because the Prophet, peace be upon him, went to the standing place immediately after the prayer.' This is the dalil.
The proof is a hadith (action of the Prophet), classified as ahad (single narration).
4
Clarify the scope
Does this ruling apply only to the imam? Is standing only valid near the mountain? The commentary clarifies that the entire field of Arafah is valid for standing.
The sunnah is for the imam to lead, but any spot in Arafah suffices for wuquf.

Source Text

قَالَ ثُمَّ يَتَوَجَّهُ إِلَى المَوقِفِ فَيَقِفُ بِقُرُبِ الْجَبَلِ وَالْقَوْمُ مَعَهُ عَقِيْبَ إِنصِرَافِهم مِنَ الصَّلوة لأنَّ النَّبِى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ رَاحَ إِلَى الْمَوْقَفِ عَقِيبَ الصَّلوةِ وَالْجَبَلُ يُسَمَّى جَبَلُ الرَّحْمَةِ والموقف موقف الأعظم

He said: Then he proceeds to the standing place and stands near the mountain, and the people with him, immediately after their departure from the prayer, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, went to the standing place immediately after the prayer. The mountain is called Jabal al-Rahmah, and the standing place is the great standing place.
Translation: He said that then he faces the standing place, so he stands near the mountain, and the people with him, immediately after the prayer, because the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, went to the standing place after the prayer. The mountain is called Jabal al-Rahmah, and the standing place is called the great standing place.
Explanation: After finishing the joining of prayers at Arafah, the imam and all the people should go to the standing place and stand near the mountain. This mountain is called Jabal al-Rahmah and the standing place is called the great standing place. The Prophet, peace be upon him, also stood near this mountain. The entire field is a place of standing.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage provides a directive (based on the Prophet's practice) for the imam and congregation to proceed to the standing place (al-mawqif) right after the combined prayer at Arafah. They are to stand near the mountain known as Jabal al-Rahmah. This mountain is the most renowned location for wuquf. The commentary emphasizes that the entire field is valid for standing, but the proximity to this particular mountain is a sunnah for the imam.

Key Terms
الموقف (al-mawqif): The place of standing on the day of Arafah, specifically at Arafah.
جبل الرحمة (Jabal al-Rahmah): The Mountain of Mercy, a specific hill in Arafah near which the Prophet stood and it is recommended to stand.

Valid Standing Places at Arafah and Muzdalifah
Defines the valid area for standing at Arafah and Muzdalifah with exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the excluded areas for wuquf at Arafah and Muzdalifah and state the Hanafi ruling on standing in those areas.

Core Idea
All of Arafah is valid for wuquf except Batn 'Urnah; all of Muzdalifah except Wadi Muhassir.

The precise boundaries of the standing places at Arafah and Muzdalifah are crucial for the validity of Hajj. This lesson clarifies the general rule and the specific exceptions based on a direct instruction of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Understanding these exceptions ensures the pilgrim avoids makruh areas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wuquf (standing) at Arafah and Muzdalifah. The ruling is that these places are valid for standing with two exceptions.
The ruling applies to the place, not the entire act of Hajj.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'All of Arafah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of 'Urnah.' A similar statement applies to Muzdalifah.
The hadith is ahad but accepted as evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'irtafi'u' (avoid) indicates prohibition of standing in Batn 'Urnah and Wadi Muhassir, while 'kulluha mawqif' establishes general permission.
The command carries weight despite being zanni al-thubut.
4
Determine the hukm level
Standing in the excluded areas is makruh tanzihi; the wuquf elsewhere is valid and mustahabb.
The Hanafi school considers it sunnah to avoid these spots.
5
Apply the rule in practice
During Hajj, the pilgrim should ensure they are within the boundaries of Arafah but not in Batn 'Urnah, and similarly for Muzdalifah.
Knowledge of these exceptions is essential for a valid Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَعَرَفَاتُ كُلُّهَا مَوْقَفٌ إِلَّا بَطْنَ عُرنَة لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَرَفَاتٌ كُلُّهَا مَوَقَفٌ وَارْتَفَعُوا عَنْ بَطَنٍ عُرْنَةٍ وَالْمُرْدَلَفَةُ كُلُّهَا مَوْقَفْ وَارْتَفَعُوا عَنْ وَادِى مُحَشَرٍ
ترجمہ: کہا اور عرفات پورا موقف ہے سواء بطن عرنہ کے۔ کیونکہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ عرفات پورا موقف ہے اور بطن عرنہ سے اونچے رہو اور مزدلفہ پورا موقف ہے اور اٹھے رہو وادی محشر سے۔
تشریح: فرمایا کہ بطن عرنہ کے علاوہ پورا عرفات موقف ہے یعنی بطن عرنہ میں کھڑا نہ ہو باقی سب کھڑے ہونے کی جگہ ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بطن عرنہ میں شیطان کو دیکھا تھا اس لئے اس مقام میں کھڑا ہونے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اسی طرح وادی محسر کے علاوہ مزدلفہ پورے کا پورا موقف ہے۔
He said: All of Arafat is a standing place except the valley of 'Urnah, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and avoid the valley of 'Urnah.' And all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Muhassir.
Translation: He said that all of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Urnah. Because the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: All of Arafat is a standing place, and stay away from Batn 'Urnah. And all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and stay away from Wadi Muhassir.
Explanation: He said that apart from Batn 'Urnah, the entire Arafat is a standing place, meaning do not stand in Batn 'Urnah; the rest is a place for standing. Some have said that the Prophet, peace be upon him, saw Satan in Batn 'Urnah, so he prohibited standing there. Similarly, apart from Wadi Muhassir, the entire Muzdalifah is a standing place.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage clarifies the boundaries of the valid standing area at Arafah and Muzdalifah. Based on a hadith, the Prophet declared all of Arafah as a valid spot for wuquf except for a specific area called Batn 'Urnah. The commentary mentions a tradition that the Prophet saw Satan there, hence the prohibition. Similarly, at Muzdalifah, the entire area except Wadi Muhassir is valid. This ruling ensures pilgrims avoid these specific locations.

Key Terms
بطن عرنة (Batn 'Urnah): A valley area within Arafah that is excluded from the standing place.
وادي محشر (Wadi Muhassir): A valley between Arafah and Muzdalifah which is excluded from standing at Muzdalifah.
