Sunnah Postures for the Imam at Wuquf: Mount and Qibla
Sunnah practices for imam's posture during wuquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two recommended practices for the imam during wuquf at Arafah and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
The imam should stand on a mount and face the Qibla—both are sunnah, not obligatory.

The standing (wuquf) at Arafah is the central rite of Hajj. The Prophet's own posture during this moment provides guidance on how the imam—and by extension the congregation—should conduct themselves. This lesson unpacks two specific sunnahs: mounting a riding beast and facing Makkah, clarifying that these are meritorious acts, not conditions of validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two recommended actions
Read the first part of the passage: the imam should stand on a riding animal (rahilah) and face the Qibla. These are distinct actions with independent proofs.
2
Locate the evidence for each
For standing on a mount: the text cites the Prophet's action (waqafa 'ala naqatihi). For facing Qibla: it cites both his action and his saying: 'Khair al-mawaqif ma istaqbilat bihi al-qiblah.'
The saying adds explicit verbal emphasis.
3
Determine the hukm level
The passage uses 'yanbaghi' (it is befitting) and 'afdal' (better), not 'wajib' or 'fard'. Standing on foot is explicitly stated as permissible (jaza). Hence the ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
The Hanafi school classifies these as confirmed sunnahs.
4
Understand the consequence of omission
If the imam stands on foot, the wuquf is valid and the hajj is complete, but he has missed the superior practice. Similarly, turning away from Qibla while facing another direction is makruh tanzihan.
There is no dam (penalty) for leaving a sunnah unless it becomes a persistent habit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ يَقِفَ بِعَرَفَةَ عَلَى رَاحِلَةٍ لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَقَفَ عَلى نَاقَتِهِ وَإِنَّ وَقَفَ عَلَى قَدَمَيْهِ جَازَ وَالْأَوَّلُ أَفْضَلَ لِمَا بَيْنَا وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَقِفَ مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةِ لِأَنَّ النَّبِى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَقَفَ كَذلِكَ وَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ خَيرُ الْمَوَاقِفِ مَا اسْتَقْبِلَتْ بِهِ الْقِبْلَةُ
ترجمہ: امام کو چاہئے کہ عرفہ میں اونٹ پر سوار ہو کر وقوف کرے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے ناقہ پر وقوف فرمایا تھا۔ اور اگر اپنے قدموں پر کھڑا ہوا تو بھی جائز ہے اور اول افضل ہے۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے اور مناسب ہے کہ قبلہ رخ ہو کر کھڑا ہو۔ اس لئے کہ حضور ایسے ہی کھڑے ہوئے ہیں اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ بہترین موقف وہ ہے جس کے ساتھ استقبال قبلہ ہو۔
تشریح: امام المسلمین کے لئے سواری پر سوار ہو کر وقوف کرنا افضل ہے کیونکہ مدنی آقا صلى الله عليه وسلم کی سنت یہی ہے لیکن اگر اپنے قدموں پر کھڑا ہو گیا تو بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور استقبال قبلہ کے ساتھ وقوف کرنا افضل ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا عمل بھی ہوا ہے اور آپ کا فرمان بھی یہی ہے۔
He said: It is befitting for the imam to stand at Arafah on a riding beast, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, stood on his she-camel. If he stands on his feet, it is permissible, but the first is better, for the reason we stated. And it is befitting that he stand facing the Qibla, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, stood like that, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The best of standing places is that in which one faces the Qibla.'
Translation: The imam should stand at Arafah riding a camel because the Prophet, peace be upon him, stood on his she-camel. If he stands on his feet, it is also permissible, but the first is better, due to the reason we mentioned. And it is appropriate to stand facing the Qibla because the Prophet stood like that and said: 'The best of standing places is that which faces the Qibla.'
Explanation: For the imam of the Muslims, standing on a mount is better because it is the sunnah of the Prophet. However, if he stands on his feet, there is no harm. Standing facing the Qibla is also better, as the Prophet did and commanded.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage outlines two recommended actions for the imam during wuquf at Arafah. First, he should stand on a riding animal (like a camel) because the Prophet did so. This is a sunnah; standing on foot is permissible (jaiz) but less meritorious (afdal). Second, he should face the Qibla, as the Prophet did and commanded that the best wuquf is facing Qibla. The commentary reinforces that these are matters of preference (afdaliyyah), not obligation.

Key Terms
راحلة (rahilah): A riding animal, typically a camel, used for travel.
مستقبل القبلة (mustaqbil al-qiblah): Facing the direction of the Qibla (towards Makkah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of the imam standing on his feet during wuquf?
A) It is invalid
B) It is permissible but less meritorious
C) It is better than riding
D) It is obligatory

Key Takeaway
Standing on a mount and facing the Qibla are confirmed sunnahs for the imam at Arafah, but standing on foot is valid and does not affect the validity of Hajj.

Imam's Du'a and Teaching at Arafah
Ruling on imam's actions at Arafah with proof from Prophetic practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions for the imam at Arafah and identify the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The imam at Arafah should make du'a and teach the rites, following the Prophet's example.

This passage from al-Hidayah instructs the imam at Arafah to engage in two important acts: supplication and instructing the pilgrims. The proof is the Prophet's own practice of raising his hands in humble supplication like a beggar. The text emphasizes flexibility in the content of du'a while recommending transmitted supplications, and highlights the importance of teaching the rituals to ensure pilgrims perform them correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prescribed acts
Locate the two actions the imam is recommended to perform: making du'a and teaching the people the rites (al-manasik).
These are not fard or wajib but sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: 'because it is narrated that the Prophet used to supplicate on the day of Arafah spreading his hands like a beggar seeking food.'
This is a hadith ahad, hence zanni al-thubut.
3
Determine the ruling level
Classify the ruling: from the evidence and the context, these acts are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended).
The Prophet's consistent practice indicates sunnah, not obligation.
4
Understand the scope of du'a
Note that the imam may supplicate with whatever he wishes (bi ma sha'), but transmitted supplications are preferred.
The text includes a lengthy du'a from Ali, which the Prophet said was most frequent.
5
Note the practical manner
Observe the recommended manner: raising hands like a beggar, indicating humility and earnestness.
This is derived from the description 'madda yadayhi kal-mustat'im al-miskin'.

وَيَدْعُوا وَيُعَلِّمُ النَّاسَ الْمَنَاسِكَ لِمَارُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ كَانَ يَدْعُو يَوْمَ عَرَفَةَ مَاذَا يَدَيْهِ كَالْمُسْتَطِعمِ الْمِسْكِينِ وَيَدْعُو بِمَا شَاء وَإِنْ وَرَدَ الْأَثَارُ بِبَعْضِ الدَّعَوَاتِ وَقَدْ أَوْرَدْنَا تَفْصِيلُهَا فِي كِتَابِنَا المُترجم بعِدَةِ الْمَنَاسِك فِي عِدَةِ مِنَ الْمَنَاسِك بتوفيق اللهِ تَعَالَى
عَنْ عَلِيِّ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَوةُ وَالسَّلامُ قَالَ أَكْثَرُ دُعَائِي وَ دُعَاءِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ مِنْ قَبْلِي عَشِيَةَ عَرَفَةَ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ لَهُ الْمُلْكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ يُحْيِي وَيُمِيتُ وَهُوَ حَيٌّ لَا يَمُوتُ بِيَدِهِ الْخَيْرُ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرُ اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْ فِي قَلْبِي نُوراً وَفِي سَمْعِى نُورًا وَفِي بَصَرِى نُوْراً اللَّهُمَّ اشْرَحْ لِي صَدْرِى وَيَسْرُ لِى أَمْرِى وَأَعُوذُبِكَ مِنْ وَسُوَاسِ الصَّدْرِ وَشَتَاءِ الْأَمْرِ وَفِتْنَةِ الْقَبْرِ اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أَعُوذُبِكَ مِنْ شَرِّ مَا يَلِجُ فِي الْبَحْرِ وَشَرِّ مَا تَهُبُّ بِهِ الرِّيَاحُ
ترجمہ: اور امام دعا مانگے اور لوگوں کو حج کے احکام سکھلائے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور عرفہ کے دن اپنے دونوں ہاتھ پھیلا کر دعا مانگنے والے مسکین کی طرح دعا کرتے تھے۔ اور جو چاہے دعا کرے اگر چہ آثار بعض دعاؤں کے ساتھ وارد ہوئے ہیں اور ہم نے ان کی تفصیل اپنی کتاب مسمى بعدة الناسك في عدة المناسک میں اللہ کی توفیق سے بیان کی ہے۔
عَنْ عَلِيٍّ: حضرت علی سے مروی ہے کہ حضور نے فرمایا: میرے اور مجھ سے پہلے کے انبیاء کا عرفہ کے دن زیادہ تر دعا یہ ہے: لا إله إلا الله ... (دعا ذکر کی گئی)
And he makes supplication and teaches the people the rites, because it is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to supplicate on the day of Arafah spreading his hands like a beggar seeking food. And he may supplicate with whatever he wishes, even though traditions have come with some specific supplications. And we have mentioned their details in our book translated as 'Iddat al-Manasik fi 'Iddat min al-Manasik', with the success of Allah the Exalted.
From 'Ali: He, peace be upon him, said: 'The most frequent supplication of mine and of the prophets before me on the evening of Arafah is: La ilaha illa Allah...' (the supplication is mentioned).
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage prescribes that the imam should both make du'a and teach the pilgrims the rituals of Hajj. The proof is the Prophet's practice of raising his hands in supplication like a needy person. The imam is free to make any du'a, but specific supplications from the Prophetic tradition are recommended. The text includes a lengthy supplication attributed to 'Ali, which the Prophet said is the most recited supplication by him and previous prophets on the evening of Arafah. The author refers to his own detailed work on Hajj rituals for more.

Key Terms
المناسك (al-manasik): The rituals and rites of Hajj and Umrah.
دعاء (du'a): Supplication, which is a recommended act at Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Teach the people the rites of Hajj
C) Deliver a long sermon
D) Remain silent

Key Takeaway
The imam at Arafah should combine supplication with teaching the pilgrims the rites, as per the Prophet's practice.

Standing Near and Behind the Imam at Arafah: Preference, Not Obligation
Instructs pilgrims to stand near and behind the imam at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing near the imam at Arafah and explain why it is a preference (afdaliyyah) rather than a requirement.

Core Idea
Stand behind the imam to face Qibla — but the entire plain of Arafah is valid for standing.

The wuquf at Arafah is the central rite of Hajj. While the entire plain is valid, the Hanafi school recommends that pilgrims stand close to the imam and behind him. This lesson unpacks the reasoning: benefiting from the imam's supplication and instruction, and automatically facing the Qibla by aligning with him. The text emphasizes this is a preference, not a pillar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being recommended and its legal level (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.).
The passage uses 'yabghi' (it is befitting), which in Hanafi terminology often indicates a sunnah or mustahab level.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Examine why standing near the imam is recommended: to benefit from his du'a and teaching.
The imam's role as teacher and leader is central.
3
Recognize the spatial arrangement
Note the instruction to stand behind the imam so that the entire congregation faces the Qibla.
This aligns with the general rule that the imam is the point of orientation.
4
Distinguish between preference and obligation
The text explicitly states this is 'bayan al-afdaliyyah' (a statement of preference). Understand that not complying does not invalidate wuquf.
The entire Arafah is a mawqif (standing place), so any location is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَبْغِي لِلنَّاسِ أَنْ يَقِفُوا بِقُرُبِ الإِمَام لِأَنَّهُ يَدْعُوَ وَيُعْلَمُ فَيَعُوا وَيَسْتَمِعُوا وَيَسْعَى أَن يَقِفُوا وَرَاءَ الْإِمَامِ لِيَكُوْنَ مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةِ وَهَذَا بَيَانُ الأفضلية لأنَّ عَرَفَاتَ كُلَّهَا مَوَقَفٌ عَلَى مَاذَكَرْنَا
ترجمہ: اور لوگوں کو چاہئے کہ وہ امام کے قریب کھڑے ہوں۔ کیونکہ امام دعا کرے گا اور احکام سکھلائے گا۔ پس لوگ یاد کریں اور کان لگا کر سنیں اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ امام کے پیچھے کھڑے ہوں تا کہ قبلہ رخ ہو جائے اور یہ بیان افضلیت ہے کیونکہ عرفات پورے کا پورا موقف ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے ذکر کیا۔
He said: It is befitting for the people to stand near the imam, because he makes supplication and teaches, so they should understand and listen. And he should endeavor that they stand behind the imam so that they face the Qibla. And this is a statement of preference, because all of Arafah is a standing place, as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage gives guidance for the congregation. They are advised to stand close to the imam to benefit from his du'a and instruction. The preferred arrangement is to stand behind the imam, so that by facing the same direction as him, they automatically face the Qibla. However, the text notes this is a matter of preference (afdaliyyah), not compulsion, because the entire plain of Arafah is valid for standing.

Key Terms
الأفضلية (al-afdaliyyah): Preference, indicating that an action is recommended but not obligatory.
موقف (mawqif): Standing place; specifically, the area of Arafah where wuquf is performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To be closer to the imam
B) To ensure they face the Qibla
C) Because it is a pillar of Hajj
D) To avoid the sun

Key Takeaway
Standing near and behind the imam at Arafah is a recommended practice (sunnah) for benefit and orientation, but the entire plain is valid for wuquf.

Imam's Posture at Wuquf: Riding and Facing Qibla
Ruling on Imam's posture at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Imam's preferred posture during Wuquf and identify the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The Imam's riding and facing Qibla at Arafah is sunnah, not wajib — preference rooted in Prophetic action and hadith.

This lesson examines a ruling from al-Hidayah on the Imam's conduct during the most important pillar of Hajj: the standing at Arafah. The text clarifies that while the Imam may stand on foot, the preferred sunnah is to ride a mount and face the Qibla, following the example of the Prophet ﷺ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling Category
Determine what action is being ruled upon (Imam's posture during Wuquf) and classify its legal status (sunnah muakkadah, not wajib).
The text uses 'afdal' (better), indicating preference.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
Find the hadith cited: 'خير المواقف ما استقبلت به القبلة' and the Prophetic practice of riding a camel.
The proof is both action (fi'l) and statement (qawl) of the Prophet.
3
Understand Afdaliyyah
Recognize that the ruling is about preference (afdaliyyah), not obligation. The act is recommended but other permissible options exist.
Afdaliyyah does not invalidate alternative valid actions.
4
Note the Permissibility of Alternatives
The text explicitly states that standing on foot is permissible (ja'iz), emphasizing that the preferred is not the only valid option.
This flexibility is characteristic of Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج
عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ خَيرُ الْمَوَاقِفِ مَا اسْتَقْبِلَتْ بِهِ الْقِبْلَةُ
ترجمہ امام کو چاہئے کہ عرفہ میں اونٹ پر سوار ہو کر وقوف کرے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے ناقہ پر وقوف فرمایا تھا۔ اور اگر اپنے قدموں پر کھڑا ہوا تو بھی جائز ہے اور اول افضل ہے۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے اور مناسب ہے کہ قبلہ رخ ہو کر کھڑا ہو۔ اس لئے کہ حضور ایسے ہی کھڑے ہوئے ہیں اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ بہترین موقف وہ ہے جس کے ساتھ استقبال قبلہ ہو۔ تشریح مسئلہ، امام المسلمین کے لئے سواری پر سوار ہو کر وقوف کرنا افضل ہے کیونکہ مدنی آقا صلى الله عليه وسلم کی سنت یہی ہے لیکن اگر اپنے قدموں پر کھڑا ہو گیا تو بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور استقبال قبلہ کے ساتھ وقوف کرنا افضل ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا عمل بھی ہوا ہے اور آپ کا فرمان بھی یہی ہے۔ چنانچہ ایک حدیث میں ہے اُن لِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ شَرَفًا وَ إِنَّ شَرَفَ الْمَجَالِسِ مَا اسْتُقْبِلَ بِهِ الْمُلَةُ اور ایک روایت میں ہے کہ اَکرَمُ الْمَجَالِسِ مَا اسْتَقْبِلَ بِهِ الْقَبْلَةُ -
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: The best standing place is that which faces the Qibla. Translation: The Imam should stand while riding a camel in Arafah, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood on his she-camel. And if he stands on his feet, it is also permissible; the first is better, due to the proof we have mentioned. And it is appropriate that he stands facing the Qibla, because the Prophet stood like that, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that the best standing is that which faces the Qibla. Elaboration: For the Imam of the Muslims, it is better to stand while riding, because this is the Sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him). But if he stands on his feet, there is no harm. And standing facing the Qibla is better, because the Prophet did so and also commanded it. Thus, a hadith states: 'Everything has a nobility, and the nobility of gatherings is that which faces the Qibla.' And in another narration: 'The most honorable gatherings are those that face the Qibla.'
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding the Imam's posture during Wuquf at Arafah. The author, based on al-Hidayah, explains that the Imam of the Muslims (the leader of the pilgrims) is recommended to stand while riding a mount (such as a camel) because the Prophet did so. However, standing on foot is also permissible. Furthermore, it is better for the Imam to face the Qibla, as the Prophet did and as indicated by hadith. The term 'Sharf al-majalis' is quoted to emphasize the virtue of facing the Qibla. The commentary clarifies that these are matters of preference (afdaliyyah), not obligation.

Key Terms
موقف (mawqif): The place of standing during Hajj, specifically at Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred action for the Imam during Wuquf at Arafah according to this text?
A) He must stand on his feet facing Qibla.
B) He should ride a mount and face Qibla.
C) He should simply sit and make du'a.
D) He should face the direction of Makkah only.

Key Takeaway
The Imam's use of a mount and facing Qibla at Arafah is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation; standing on foot remains valid.

Imam's Du'a and Teaching During Wuquf
Ruling on Imam's du'a and teaching during Wuquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the Imam's du'a and teaching during Wuquf and identify the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The Imam's du'a and teaching at Arafah is a confirmed Sunnah, grounded in the Prophet's own practice.

In this passage, al-Marghinani discusses the actions of the Imam during the standing at Arafah. The Imam is not only to supplicate but also to instruct the pilgrims in the rites of Hajj. This ruling is based on the Prophet's own conduct, as transmitted in authentic reports. The text also provides a specific supplication reported from 'Ali, illustrating the type of du'a recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is the Imam required to do? State the ruling level (sunnah, wajib, etc.).
The passage uses the imperative tone, but the ruling is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
What proof does the author cite for the Imam's actions?
The dalil is a hadith describing the Prophet's posture and supplication at Arafah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the Prophet's practice serve as evidence for the Imam's recommended actions?
The Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates desirability, not obligation, in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the scope of the Imam's discretion
Can the Imam choose any supplication, or must he use specific ones?
The text says 'yad'u bima sha' (he supplicates as he wishes), though transmitted du'as are also cited.
5
Recognize the author's reference to his own work
Why does the author mention his other book?
To show that detailed supplications are compiled elsewhere, but the basic ruling is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام دعا اور تعلیم کا کام سرانجام دیتار ہے
وَيَدْعُوا وَيُعَلِّمُ النَّاسَ الْمَنَاسِكَ لِمَارُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ كَانَ يَدْعُو يَوْمَ عَرَفَةَ مَاذَا يَدَيْهِ كَالْمُسْتَطِعم المسكيْنِ وَيَدْعُو بِمَا شَاء وَإِنْ وَرَدَ الْأَثَارُ بِبَعْضِ الدَّعَوَاتِ وَقَدْ أَوْرَدْنَا تَفْصِيلُهَا فِي كِتَابِنَا المُترجم به دة الْمَنَاسِك فِي عِدَةِ مِنَ الْمَنَاسِك بتوفيق اللهِ تَعَالَى
ترجمہ اور امام دعا مانگے اور لوگوں کو حج کے احکام سکھلائے ۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور عرفہ کے دن اپنے دونوں ہاتھ پھیلا کر دمانا مانگنے والے مسکین کی طرح دعا کرتے تھے۔ اور جو چاہے دعا کرے اگر چہ آثار بعض دعاؤں کے ساتھ وارد ہوئے ہیں اور ہم نے ان کی تفصیل اپنی کتاب مُسَمًّى بِعَدَةِ النَّاسِك فِي عِدَةِ الْمَنَاسِک میں اللہ کی توفیق سے بیان کی ہے۔
تشریح جن دعاؤں کے بارے میں آثار وارد ہوئے ہیں ان میں ایک اثر حضرت علی کا ہے۔ عَنْ عَلِيِّ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَوةُ وَالسَّلامُ قَالَ أَكْثِرُ دُعَائِي وَ دُعَاءِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ مِنْ قَبْلِي عَشِيَةَ عَرَفَةَ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ لَهُ الْمُلكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ يُحْيِي وَيُمِيتُ وَهُوَ حَيٌّ لَا يَمُوتُ بِيَدِهِ الْخَيْرُ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرُ اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلَ فِي قَلْبِي نُوراً وَ فِي سَمْعِى نُورًا وَ فِي بَصَرِى نُوْراً اللَّهُمَّ اشْرَحْ لِي صَدْرِى وَيَسْرُ لِى اَمْرِى وَ أَعُوذُبِكَ مِنْ وَسُوَاسِ الصَّدْرِ وَشَتَاءِ الأمرِ وَفِيةِ الْقَبْرِ اللَّهُمَّ إلى أعُوذُبِكَ مِنْ شَرِّ مَا يَلحُ فِي الْبَحْرِ وَشَرِ مَاتَهَبْ بِهِ الرِّباحُ -
The Imam makes du'a and teaches the people the rituals (manasik). Because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to make du'a on the Day of Arafah spreading his hands like a needy beggar, and he would supplicate as he wished, although reports have come with specific supplications. We have detailed them in our book titled 'Uddat al-Nasik fi 'Uddat al-Manasik', by the grace of Allah. Translation: And the Imam makes du'a and teaches the people the rulings of Hajj. Because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) on the day of Arafah would spread his hands like a beggar seeking food and would supplicate as he wished. Even though reports have come with particular supplications, we have detailed them in our book 'Uddat al-Nasik fi 'Uddat al-Manasik' by the grace of Allah. Elaboration: Among the supplications for which reports exist, one is from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): from 'Ali that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Most of my supplication and the supplication of the prophets before me on the evening of Arafah is: La ilaha illallah, wahdahu la sharika lah, lahul mulku wa lahul hamdu, yuhyi wa yumit, wa huwa hayyun la yamutu, biyadihil khayru, wa huwa 'ala kulli shay'in qadir. Allahumma ej'al fi qalbi nuran, wa fi sam'i nuran, wa fi basari nuran. Allahumma ishrah li sadri wa yassir li amri, wa a'udhu bika min waswasis sadri wa shata'il amri, wa fitnatil qabr. Allahumma inni a'udhu bika min sharri ma yaliju fil bahri, wa sharri ma tahubbu bihir riyah.'
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the Imam's actions during Wuquf at Arafah. The Imam is recommended to make du'a and teach the pilgrims the rituals. The evidence is the Prophet's practice of supplicating with his hands raised like a beggar. The Imam may supplicate with any words, but there are specific transmitted supplications (athar), one of which is quoted from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). The author notes that he has compiled these in another work. The Hanafi school holds that this teaching is a sunnah, not a fard, and the Imam should focus on supplication and instruction.

Key Terms
آثار (athar): Reports or narrations, specifically here referring to transmitted supplications from the Prophet or Companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the Imam recommended to do during Wuquf besides supplicating?
A) Lead the salah.
B) Teach the people the Hajj rituals.
C) Give a sermon (khutbah).
D) Recite the Quran loudly.

Key Takeaway
The Imam's du'a and teaching during Wuquf is a confirmed sunnah based on the Prophet's practice, and he may supplicate freely or use transmitted supplications.
